Current Affairs Commentary

The Change of the French Left-Wing Cabinet and the Fate of the Gold Standard 19

— By You

The French Daladier cabinet, due to the failure of the French central government's budget balancing plan to pass in the Chamber of Deputies, resigned en masse on the 24th. The Daladier cabinet's fiscal policy was based on tax increases and reduced government spending as a prerequisite, and resolutely rejected the adoption of inflation. After the change of the French cabinet, what kind of changes will occur in the French finances, especially the fate of the French gold standard? It seems to be a major issue in the current global economic panic.

The French Radical Party's Daladier cabinet, since succeeding Herriot and Poincaré one after another on January 31st of this year, has been in power for only nine months. During his tenure, Mr. Daladier has consistently adhered to the principle of supporting monetary contraction and maintaining the gold standard in all economic policies related to finance and currency. The formation of the European Gold Standard Alliance in conjunction with Italy, Switzerland, the Netherlands, and Belgium is clear evidence of this. However, the collapse of his cabinet has other significant reasons. According to the Havas Paris dispatch on the 24th, one of the provisions of the fiscal bill submitted by the government stipulated that a fixed income of 6% tax should be levied from public and private sector employees, regardless of salary or benefits. However, the majority of the Socialist Party firmly expressed their opposition, making a compromise difficult. The majority party in the French Chamber of Deputies that supports the government is composed of the Radical Party and the Socialist Party. Now that the majority of the Socialist Party cannot cooperate with the government, and the government regards its policy as having no room for hesitation, the cabinet can only resign en masse. Therefore, the essence of this cabinet crisis lies here and not elsewhere.

From another aspect of this cabinet crisis, the collapse of the current French cabinet authorities does not necessarily mean that France is about to adopt inflation. Because, based on the national conditions of France, the people have not forgotten the pain of the devaluation of the franc after the war, and the political parties do not dare to make such a proposal that is clearly contrary to public opinion. Therefore, judging from the general situation, the question of whether the French gold standard can be maintained does not seem to be triggered by the change of cabinet. Although French finances are in a time of panic, the deficit in next year's revenue and expenditure will reach 600 billion francs (currently equivalent to about 75 million pounds in English gold). In the future, when a new cabinet is established, it may be possible to adopt inflation, but this cannot be predicted as an inevitable trend.

The fact that France and the gold standards of various European countries still stand today is indeed a remarkable event. However, the future determinant of the fate of the gold standard does not lie in the changes in domestic politics, but only in the changes in American monetary policy. The day before yesterday, the US president clearly announced during his broadcast that the United States will raise prices. The means are, on the one hand, to buy newly produced gold domestically, and on the other hand, to manipulate exchange rates in the world's major financial markets. As a result, the US dollar will inevitably tend to fall, and then prices can be raised. In addition to the English gold following suit, the French franc will inevitably suffer significant pressure. In addition, in the past three years, French export trade has decreased by 50%. If it were not for the French colonies to absorb its surplus commodities to ease the outbreak of the crisis, the French gold standard would have been unsustainable. Therefore, as of today, the fate of the franc is almost tied to how the two major forces of the gold pound and the gold yuan compete for supremacy in the world currency market. This is what can be predicted.

Urgent Legal and Political Crisis: Efforts to Resolve It; Sarraut Willing to Attempt Forming a New Cabinet; Daladier Likely to Head the Army or Foreign Affairs; Flandin's Position Increasingly Precarious; Threat of Financial Dictatorship 20

(Paris) After lengthy consultations with his friends, Sarraut has indicated to the French President his willingness to undertake the formation of a cabinet. (Reuter, 25th)

(Paris) The French President this afternoon urged Sarraut to assume the premiership. Sarraut is a senator and served as Minister of the Navy in the Daladier cabinet. During the financial panic of 1928, Premier Poincaré relied on him as his right-hand man. It is widely expected that Daladier will head the Army or Foreign Affairs in the new government. (Reuter, 25th)

(Paris) The French political crisis not only endangers the gold standard but also the democratic system. The general public is questioning whether France can find a strong leader. The financial failures of the Herriot, Painlevé, and Daladier cabinets demonstrate the impossibility of joint governance by the Radical and Socialist parties. Daladier's political skill and strategy have earned him widespread recognition, but the majority of Socialist deputies, led by Blum, while internally divided, do not support the gold standard and favor inflation, consistently ignoring Daladier's arguments about the necessity of balancing the budget. The only solution now seems to be to form a new cabinet with parties other than the Socialist Party, but such a government may not last long. A significant part of France's financial difficulties stems from taxpayers refusing to pay income taxes. A certain parliamentarian, in a recent debate, estimated that unpaid income taxes are approximately twice the budget deficit. Flandin has not yet been significantly affected, but his future is quite concerning. If the cabinet fails again over the budget proposal, it may lead to a financial dictatorship. (Reuter, 25th)

Rome The fall of the Daladier government has caused great alarm in Italian political circles. It is believed that the European situation will completely change. With the French right-wing coming into power, it is feared that the French government will adopt a more assertive attitude towards diplomatic and political issues, eliminating any hope for Franco-German understanding. Without German cooperation, the continuation of the Disarmament Conference is absolutely hopeless. Italian newspapers state that Daladier's failure and the possible decline of the franc will have unfavorable impacts on the overall European situation. However, political circles view the French cabinet crisis as further proof of the unsuitability of the parliamentary system to the times. (National Telegram, 25th)

Disarmament Leadership Meeting; Chairman Henderson Suggests: General Committee Adjourn Until December 4th; Core Leadership Continues Work on Draft Treaty; US and Italy Oppose Indefinite Postponement; Britain Forced to Change Initial Stance 21

(Geneva) At 3:40 PM today, during the Disarmament Conference leadership meeting, Henderson suggested that the General Committee should be extended, but no later than December 4th, stating that during the extension, the core leadership could continue drafting the final version of the convention. (Reuter, 25th)

(London) Although British officials favor a long-term postponement of the Disarmament Conference, the British government cannot but change its intentions due to the opposition of Italy and the United States. Most relevant to this matter was the visit of the Italian Ambassador to Britain, Grandi, to the Foreign Office yesterday. Last week, the British government's intention leaned towards a long-term postponement, but after exchanging views with continental countries, especially France, it now intends to continue the Disarmament Conference's work, albeit on a smaller scale and with a temporary mechanism instead of its current structure. When the Italian Ambassador, Grandi, visited the Foreign Office, he clearly stated that the Italian government hoped the Disarmament Conference would continue its efforts, and the shorter the postponement, the better. Sources here explain the Roman government's intention as follows: the Four-Power Pact is currently being tested, and if the Disarmament Conference is postponed indefinitely, the treaty will be proven invalid, and the success of Italian policy will be affected, which is something the Italian government does not want to hear. As for the United States, it also hopes that the Disarmament Conference will continue its work so that the United States can continue to maintain its influence and mission, along with its observer status. This would not be possible with an indefinite postponement. President Roosevelt personally stated this. Britain is well aware of the views of Italy and the United States, so although British officials favor a long-term postponement, given the situation on all sides, they cannot but change their initial stance. (Havas, 24th)

Hitler's Important Broadcast Speech; Claims Germany Suffers Greatly Due to the Treaty; Unwilling to Submit to Foreign Powers; Maintains National Honor 22

(Berlin) With the German Reichstag elections approaching, tens of thousands of Nazi Party members gathered at the sports field today for an election rally. Hitler delivered a speech at the venue, which was broadcast via radio. Gatherings were held in over sixty locations throughout Berlin, all of which could hear the speech. First, Propaganda Minister Goebbels spoke, saying that the German nation's loyalty to Hitler is trustworthy and unsurpassed today. Then, Hitler spoke, saying that the government will strive to fulfill its responsibilities and will never yield. He continued, "Why does the world not give us peace? The greatest suffering Germany has endured comes from the Treaty of Versailles. In the National Socialist revolution, no more than fifty Germans were sacrificed, but they were all shameless individuals. As for those sacrificed by the Treaty of Versailles, it is no fewer than several each year." Hitler also said that foreign rumors about Germany practicing tyranny are completely unfounded. Hitler said, "Our party's enemies hate us; this is our only misfortune. Germans who flee abroad publish brown books to slander the German government. These exiles are all scoundrels, and their actions of defaming the country through printed materials cannot be tolerated by any government. Germany, to preserve its reputation, must remember what Germans fought for during the Great War, which was to protect Germany's honor. The movement to ostracize Germany is an intolerable insult. If the words used to criticize German cabinet members were applied to the British Privy Councillor Baldwin, would the British people be able to tolerate it?" Hitler concluded by saying that Germany's ambition is to restore friendly relations between all nations and does not want their feuds to remain unresolved forever. (Havas, 24th)

British Newspaper Correspondent in Germany Arrested 23

(Berlin) The Munich correspondent for the British Daily Telegraph was arrested today, presumably because his report on Chancellor Hitler's speech in Kiel offended the authorities. (Reuter, 24th)

Canadian Nickel Exports Increase Significantly; For Use in Manufacturing Arms 24

Ottawa A representative of the German I.G. Farben company arrived here today to purchase a large quantity of Canadian nickel. It is claimed that the company is currently developing a nickel plating method. Nickel is a key material for manufacturing arms, and exports have increased significantly recently. In the first six months of this year, a total of 513,000 dan (approximately 112 pounds per dan) of nickel were exported, compared to only 128,000 dan during the same period last year. Germany imported a total of 2,557 dan in the first half of last year, but this has more than doubled in the first half of this year. (Reuter, 24th)

US New Monetary Policy: Gradual Inflation; Fluctuating Gold Prices; A New Speculative Frenzy in the Market 25

(New York) Tonight, local bankers and market participants plunged into complete confusion upon hearing news from Washington that some radical inflationists had interpreted the President's new monetary plan as a practical move towards inflation. It is reported that inflationists within Congress, along with representatives from various cotton and agricultural groups, met with Senator Thomas to discuss the government's new plan. After Thomas explained his views, everyone agreed that the President's intention in controlling the monetary plan was simply to implement orderly inflation. As a result, a resolution was adopted supporting the government's new monetary policy. Therefore, market traders hold differing opinions on the fluctuations of gold prices after the initial announcement of domestic gold prices. Some still insist on their original claim that gold prices will not fluctuate significantly, but others also say that the inflationists' resolution is not meaningless. Furthermore, Secretary of Agriculture Wallace announced a processing tax of 25 cents per bushel on corn products, including cornstarch, corn flakes, cornmeal, corn grits, and syrup, further increasing the confusion. In addition, Wallace ordered the collection of opinions to determine whether the plan to purchase $350 million worth of pork, grains, and other foods to distribute to the unemployed would raise prices, and also reduce the extent to which the public cuts back on consumption, as Wallace has received many complaints that the wheat processing tax actually reduces consumption. Today's various government actions have sparked a new speculative frenzy. More cautious traders say that the market will be chaotic unless opinions can be somewhat unified before the market opens. (National Telegram, 24th)

President Pays Attention to Silver Reserves: Formulating Practical Procedures 26

(Washington) According to reliable sources, President Roosevelt has now launched the gold plan and will immediately turn his attention to silver. Congressmen who advocate for the restoration of silver coinage say that President Roosevelt is considering the silver issue and will hold a meeting soon to formulate practical procedures. Senator Pittman told people today, expounding on the urgency of the silver issue. Others involved with silver hope that the authorities will set the price of silver at 90 cents per ounce, placing gold and silver on an equal footing. President Roosevelt supports maintaining silver, but has not yet decided on the best way to achieve this goal. (Reuter, 25th)

Fixed Official Price for Mined Gold: Large-Scale Purchases Will Begin Immediately 27

(Washington) This morning, the Reconstruction Finance Corporation (RFC) announced that, in accordance with President Roosevelt's new monetary plan, it would set the official purchase price for newly mined gold at $31.64 per ounce of pure gold. This price is $1.55 higher than the Treasury Department's recent price for gold sold abroad and 23 cents higher than the price of gold in London. Based on the London-New York exchange rate of $4.78, the price of gold in London is only $31.13. It is because the RFC is a corporate organization and is not subject to the gold standard law that President Roosevelt specifically ordered the RFC and the Treasury Department to buy and sell gold. In contrast, the Treasury Department, due to the law stipulating that the government must purchase gold at a fixed price, may be suspected of violating the law if it sets a new price. The gold price announced today was decided in a meeting at the Treasury Department between RFC Chairman Jesse Jones, Undersecretary of the Treasury Acheson, and Agricultural Adjustment Administration Director Morgenthau. Jones claimed that the purchase price of newly mined gold would be paid with 90-day bonds issued by the RFC. (National Telegram, 25th)

The Nation Eagerly Awaits Measures for the Monetary Plan 28

(New York) Today, American markets and businesses nationwide are eagerly awaiting President Roosevelt's measures regarding the gold standard. The actions of President Roosevelt and monetary authorities before the market opens tomorrow are the sole topic of discussion among bankers and brokers here. RFC Chairman Jones and other related personnel will meet at the Treasury Department in Washington tomorrow morning at around 9:00 AM to decide on the first official price for newly mined gold. All parties now recognize that this new official price is the first practical indication of the government's intentions and therefore attach great importance to it. Some bankers and brokers in New York have even temporarily leased telephone lines in order to obtain the news first. Today, the Treasury Department has indicated that the RFC will stop transporting gold to foreign markets after purchasing it, and stated that the government's official price may be higher than the world price, so miners do not need to transport gold abroad. (National Telegram, 24th)

Moderate Tariff Increases to Encourage Domestic Price Increases 29

(Washington) Today, in order to encourage price increases, President Roosevelt ordered the implementation of the tariff regulations in the National Industrial Recovery Act (NIRA). According to the Act, the President is authorized to impose compensatory taxes on raw materials, increase tariffs on other goods, or completely prohibit imports if domestic products are at risk from foreign competition. President Roosevelt now believes that domestic goods are facing excessive foreign competition, so he wants to selectively increase tariffs or completely prohibit imports after special investigations. This investigation will be initiated by NIRA Administrator Johnson within a few days. Today, officials at the NIRA admitted that the NIRA, like inflationary methods, cannot cure all ills. Therefore, if the industrial sector is to continue adding employees, increasing wages, and finding markets, the government must give the plan its full force. Since the government decided to resume purchasing gold, the possibility of increasing import tariffs on many manufactured goods has arisen. The outside world also interprets this move differently. Some bankers in New York believe that this can raise prices and no longer suppress the gold standard. A banker in Washington said that the President clearly wants to abandon the method of suppressing the gold standard and wants to increase tariffs so that the gold standard can at least remain at its current level. However, others also say that this move has nothing to do with currency and is only because the progress of the recovery plan is too slow. (National Telegram, 24th)

Impact on War Debts: Differing Speculation Abroad 30

(London). There is much speculation on both sides of the Atlantic about whether President Roosevelt's new monetary policy will have an adverse effect on the Anglo-American war debt negotiations. According to a New York dispatch to Washington, the hope for a permanent resolution of the Anglo-American war debt has disappeared because the dollar is unstable, and negotiations are pointless at present. But practically speaking, it seems too early to predict the impact of the President's policy today. Londoners believe that while the new monetary policy may cause fluctuations, President Roosevelt's goal is to establish a dollar that does not change its purchasing power or debt repayment capacity in the next thirty years. No one wants drastic fluctuations in the dollar exchange rate either. Therefore, superficial fluctuations may not be enough to prevent the resolution of the war debt issue. Although bankers within the United States have expressed dismay at President Roosevelt's actions, the American banking community in London does not hold this view. They believe that the new policy is a step towards the establishment of an American exchange equalization fund (and that, when the fund is established in the future) it will de facto create stability in the Anglo-American exchange rate. (Reuter, 24th)

Farmers' Strike for Sales: Struggle for Timely Purchases Lacks Vitality 31

(New York) Reno, President of the Farmers' Holiday Association, criticized President Roosevelt's monetary policy, saying it was purely fanciful, and the farmers' struggle would not cease until their demands were guaranteed. Nebraska Governor Bryan also spoke out for the farmers, saying that the farmers' throats are currently being cut. This shows the tension of the farmers' emotions. Farmers' pickets are currently prohibiting grain trucks from traveling, and although some still anticipate that the farmers' strike will not greatly affect the food supply of the cities, all believe that the success or failure of the recovery movement largely depends on this issue. It is heard that farmers everywhere are currently unwilling to shop at stores that display the Blue Eagle recovery emblem. Furthermore, stores have been hit hard by the large increase in wages. It is widely believed that the "buy now" movement has now lost its vitality. President Roosevelt has ordered an immediate investigation into market prices, and the authorities will likely strictly prohibit hoarding and profiteering and immediately provide farmers with loans secured by grains. General public opinion believes that President Roosevelt is now being gradually forced towards an inflationary policy. Many political forces are driving him to do so, and the greatest force is the farmers, who deeply believe that the only way to save the countryside is through a cheap dollar. (Reuter, 24th)

Hirota Emphasizes the Selection of an Ambassador to the United States; Debuchi Scheduled to Return to Japan 32

(Tokyo) According to a cable received from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Ambassador to the United States Debuchi Katsuji is scheduled to leave the United States on November 24th to return to Japan. It has now been confirmed that Debuchi's resignation after returning home is certain. Foreign Minister Hirota is currently considering candidates for the successor ambassador. It is heard that his selection policy seems to aim for the Second Washington Conference in 1935. It is heard that the Foreign Minister's views are generally as follows: The Second Washington Conference will discuss naval disarmament, and Japan is also prepared to attend the conference and adjust Japanese-American relations. The new Ambassador to the United States must be qualified to handle all of these tasks. Therefore, the Foreign Minister intends to select a first-class individual who is knowledgeable about the situation in the Far East and Japanese-American relations, and who possesses skillful means and high intelligence. Talents who meet the above conditions can be sought from political, financial, and other circles, and are not limited to diplomats. (Nichi Ren Telegram, 25th)

(Tokyo) The responsibilities of the Ambassador to the United States who will succeed Ambassador Debuchi are, needless to say, very heavy. Especially since the Manchurian Incident, there has been a need to repair the broken Japanese-American relations in a satisfactory manner. At the same time, the new Ambassador must undertake preparatory work for the next Disarmament Conference in 1935 and must attend the conference as one of the Empire's main plenipotentiaries. The responsibilities are very heavy. Foreign Minister Hirota is carefully considering the selection of a successor. It is heard that the Foreign Minister is evaluating candidates based on the following guidelines: (1) The successor Ambassador to the United States must be someone who is endorsed by everyone inside and outside the country and need not be a diplomat within the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (2) To refresh the personnel of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and create a new spirit between Japan and the United States, experienced veterans should be avoided, and promising newcomers should be adopted. From this point of view, Ambassador to Germany Nagai and Ambassador to Italy Yoshida, who are so-called veterans, cannot be considered newcomers. Minister to the Netherlands Saito Hiroshi can be considered a young and promising diplomat, but there is a need to consider the future. Matsuoka Yosuke, outside the Ministry, also has shortcomings and cannot be considered the most suitable candidate. As a result, it is also possible that Sugimura Yotaro, who is knowledgeable about international affairs, may be appointed, as Minister Sugimura has served as Deputy Secretary-General of the League of Nations for many years, and internationally he is recognized for his consummate personality and skilled ability. Ambassador Debuchi also sent a telegram to Tokyo yesterday, saying that he would depart San Francisco on November 24th and arrive in Tokyo on December 10th. (Dentsu Telegram, 25th)

US-Russia Resumption of Diplomatic Relations Negotiations Will Involve Issues with Japan: Russia Hopes to Establish Understanding with the US 33

(Moscow) Observers believe that the United States' motive for recognizing Soviet Russia is likely the tense situation in the Far East, and the Americans also believe that Soviet Russia wants to establish friendly relations with the US to consolidate its own position. It is now heard that Litvinov will prepare everything when he goes to Washington in order to seek some kind of American understanding regarding Japan. (Reuter, 24th)

Japanese Political Parties' Joint Constitutional Protection Movement; Members of the Minseito and Seiyukai Parties in Repeated Contact; Hoping to Realize Before the December Parliamentary Session; Reaction Against the Military Clique Controlling the Political Situation 34

(Tokyo) Minseito's Kobashi, Tomita, Tawara, and others believe that to open up the current extraordinary situation and uphold constitutional politics, the political parties must cooperate with each other. As a result of repeated negotiations with Seiyukai members, it has been decided that Minseito's Tomita and Tawara will meet with Seiyukai's Kuhara and Shimada within the next few days to exchange concrete opinions on the issue of political party merger. However, there is no understanding between the leaders of the two parties on this issue, and whether its future can be realized is still questionable. (Nichi Ren Telegram, 25th)

(Tokyo) The issue of political party alliance is becoming more concrete after discussions between Seiyukai's Kuhara and Shimada and Minseito's Tomita and Tawara. Therefore, Education Minister Hatoyama also visited Prime Minister Suzuki at 8:30 AM on the 25th to conduct important consultations on the policies that the party headquarters should take regarding this issue, and left around 9:00 AM. Chief Secretary Shimada also visited Suzuki after 9:00 AM to report in detail on the situation of the two parties' discussions and exchange of opinions and discuss countermeasures. On the other hand, Secretary General Yamaguchi also visited the Education Minister at the same time to discuss this issue and then consulted with Shimada at the headquarters. On the Seiyukai side, it is advocated that they jointly study national policies, restore the credibility of political parties, and work together to open up the current situation and seek political party alliance. The aim is to make opinions as consistent as possible from the party's standpoint, but the so-called national one-party system cannot be endorsed. Its executives all tend to hold this view. Therefore, an atmosphere of political party alliance is being created with the aforementioned meaning. If the Minseito understands the true spirit of this, it will not hesitate to cooperate. However, Minseito's Tomita and Tawara have also reported the details of this case to their top executives. In order to seek their understanding, Ohara Osamu, Kawasaki, Raimogi, Masada, Machida and others summoned a meeting on the 25th, but it failed to materialize due to various reasons. Within the Minseito, regarding this plan for the two parties to negotiate, it is said that it is still the Seiyukai's internal strategy and that there is a fear that it will turn into a movement to overthrow the current cabinet and promote fascist tendencies, so they all take a negative attitude towards it. Except for Tomita and Tawara, the other members of the Minseito are all making pessimistic observations on the future of the issue. The current Minseito is only acting as a gathering for exchanging opinions, and there are still considerable twists and turns in the future of the issue. (Nichi Ren Telegram, 25th)

(Tokyo) The so-called political party alliance movement launched by the Seiyukai and Minseito has recently resurfaced. Although the military authorities outwardly approve of its objectives, they feel that it is difficult to realize and are paying attention to its future development. The political party alliance movement was originally intended to address the lack of capacity and loss of credibility of the existing political parties by forming a rational alliance to enhance their capabilities, regain their credibility, and hope to rectify the current situation. If this situation is the true intention, then its objectives are extremely commendable. However, the leaders of the existing political parties are still blinded by traditional customs and lack foresight regarding the general trend. Even with this movement today, it is difficult to suddenly expect its effects. On the one hand, it is said that the reason why political parties are moving to unite is as a pressure tactic against the military authorities, or as a means for the Seiyukai to restrain the Minseito. If it contains such impure motives, then its actions will ultimately fail, which can be easily asserted. In short, the existing political parties must completely abandon the traditional party interests, party strategies, and all such ingrained habits, and they must resolve to serve the country and strive to achieve their objectives. If this is not the case, then the success of the movement will be absolutely impossible. (Nichi Ren Telegram, 25th)

The Future of the Puppet State 35

(Tokyo) According to recent news from Chinese newspapers, the Japanese government has decided to abolish the "Manchu Government," annexing Manchuria into Japanese territory, and has set January 1 of next year as the date for implementation. This claim has been denied by Japanese officials and other figures, and foreigners who are interested in politics in Japan do not believe this claim or pay much attention to it. However, while Japan's annexation of Manchuria is not credible in the current environment, there will be considerable changes and developments within "Manchukuo" in the near future, at least. There are two recent facts that are particularly relevant to this matter: one is that Zhao Xinbo, President of the "Manchukuo" Legislative Yuan, recently came to Japan to study Japanese constitutional politics and the organization of its parliament; and the other is the appointment of Doihara as the head of the Shenyang Special Affairs Agency on October 17. When Zhao Xinbo came to Japan, he told reporters that "Manchukuo" had decided to adopt a constitutional monarchy sooner or later, with Puyi as king. Therefore, they will be studying the Japanese Imperial House Law together. Zhao will stay in Japan for about a year and then return to Manchukuo to draft a new constitution based on his research in Japan. From this event, it can be seen that the administrative organization of "Manchukuo" is likely to be changed to a constitutional monarchy, but it is not Japan annexing Manchuria. (Reuter, 23rd)

(Changchun) The "Manchu Government" will implement a centralized system from next year, stipulating the abolition of the five-province system and dividing the provinces into several small administrative districts under the direct jurisdiction of the central government. (Reuter, 25th)

(Tokyo) Minister to Sweden Yada Shichitaro is scheduled to return home on leave at the end of this month. After returning home, there is talk of inviting him to serve as a councillor in "Manchukuo" and as the highest advisor on diplomatic matters for Manchukuo. (Dentsu Telegram, 25th)

New International Tin Agreement to be Signed in London Tomorrow; Negotiations with China Underway 37

(London) The Financial Times reports that, according to reliable Dutch sources, the new International Tin Agreement will be signed in London on Friday, increasing production limits to 40 percent. The new agreement will last for three years, effective from January 1 of next year. Vietnam is said to be joining the plan, and negotiations with Burma and the Chinese government have now begun. It is also said that the limits of the new agreement will take into account the materials contained in the minerals exported by each country. If a country that does not join the new agreement produces 25 percent of the world's total tin production in six consecutive months, the signatory countries may withdraw from the agreement with six months' notice. There is currently no immediate risk of a sudden shortage of tin supply. (October 25, Reuters)

Chinese Compatriots in the Federated Malay States Petition for Repeal of Rice Import Tax 38

Singapore Since October 17, when the government of the Federated Malay States imposed a tax of 15 cents per picul on imported rice, it has caused anxiety among the Chinese here, as the Chinese account for 65 percent of the total population of Malaya. According to Chinese leaders, it is unwise for the government to suddenly increase taxes at a time when wages are low and unemployment is still serious. The Director of Agriculture said in his report that the rice tax burden per person per month is only 7 cents, but Chinese rice importers say that customs duties, freight, warehouse rent, and the increased rice tax amount to at least 30 cents. Chinese and other Asians residing here are preparing to jointly petition the authorities to repeal this tax until the Federated Malay States can become self-sufficient, and at the same time, request the government to subsidize Chinese farmers and allow Chinese farmers to enjoy the same rights as local farmers. (October 24, Reuters)

Guangdong Promotes Cotton Weaving Industry, Hires British Consultant 39

Manchester Walter Hanbury Belgrave, former manager of a yarn factory, has been hired by the Guangdong government as a yarn factory consultant for a two-year contract. The Guangdong government plans to build a yarn factory using all British-made machinery and British factory management methods to resist competition from Japanese goods. The Manchester newspaper wrote in an article that the Dutch East Indies, Persia, and Egypt have also had similar plans recently, which may affect Lancashire's second largest overseas market. (October 24, Reuters)

Small Coastal Steamer Lost in Storm off Singapore; 28 Drowned, Mostly Chinese 40

Singapore The small steamer Trang Tsu, which travels between coastal ports of Singapore, sank in a storm on Sunday. Of the 37 crew members, 28 drowned, mostly Chinese. The nine survivors have landed here. (October 25, Reuters)

One Birth, Seven Sons 41

▲Reuters, October 24, from British Guiana (north of Brazil): A woman here gave birth to seven sons last night. According to the attending physician, this is a groundbreaking event in medical history.
