Joint Statement from the Postal Workers' Unions to All Sectors Regarding the Liu-Yang Embezzlement Case 164

A joint statement from the Shanghai Postal Workers' Unions to all sectors regarding the Liu Shufan and Yang Jianping embezzlement case at the former Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau: A Public Statement to All Sectors of the Country: According to reports, the Control Yuan has impeached Liu Shufan and Yang Jianping, the former directors of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, for dereliction of duty, embezzlement, and illegal activities. Furthermore, the "Shen Bao" of this port published on the 16th of this month reported that Liu Shufan and Yang Jianping, the former directors of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, were impeached by the Control Yuan for dereliction of duty and embezzlement, and that the Central Public Servants Disciplinary Committee and the Shanghai District Court had successively conducted investigations according to law, finding that Liu and Yang were suspected of major embezzlement. It was also said that the most important point in this case was the discrepancy in the amount paid for the purchase of land, amounting to as much as 150,000 yuan. Since this news was disseminated, not only have our two postal workers' unions been deeply indignant, but people from all walks of life should also be shocked to hear of it. The Savings and Remittance Bureau is a savings institution for the hard-earned money of the common people, and Liu Shufan and Yang Jianping were administrative officials appointed by the government. The importance of the matter and the seriousness of the case are by no means comparable to ordinary news. There are two points that our two unions want to address: (1) The Savings and Remittance Bureau was established in 1930 by separating the savings and remittance departments from the General Post Office. The original purpose of establishing these two departments was to utilize the stable position of the postal service and its already established reputation to facilitate the public and promote thrift. In other words, the assets of the postal service and its operating surplus were used as a guarantee to promote the cause of national prosperity and benefit the people. Furthermore, the savings and remittance business was handled by postal personnel in the past. Because postal personnel had extensive experience in handling savings and remittance business and were well aware of the close relationship between savings and remittance business and the postal service, the smoothness and prudence of operations were self-evident. From this, it can be seen that there was not only no need to separate the postal savings and remittance business from the postal service itself, but there was also the fact that it could not be separated. Therefore, we cannot but regard the separation of the Savings and Remittance Bureau from the Postal Bureau as a major mistake. Furthermore, if the Savings and Remittance Bureau had not been separated in the first place, Liu and Yang's embezzlement would not have been possible. This is the first point we want to make. (2) Regarding the issue of personnel recruitment, the postal service has a very strict system for personnel recruitment. Appointments are based on principles, promotions and demotions are orderly, and the lives of current personnel are guaranteed. With these factors in place, postal service personnel are able to remain loyal to their duties and not harbor ulterior motives. However, since the establishment of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, the bureau has completely destroyed the good personnel system that the Postal Bureau has always used. As a result, low-level staff were promoted through connections, filling every available position, while key officials came and went, with no consistency in their appointments. It is estimated that at the beginning of the bureau's establishment, no less than 20 or 30 people entered the bureau through the kinship of the bureau director. Furthermore, the director of the bureau has changed three times in a short period of time. A national economic institution has been transformed into an arena for bureaucratic politicians to compete for power. It is naturally impossible to expect the staff at all levels to devote themselves to their work. Therefore, we cannot but regard the government's appointment of the Savings and Remittance Bureau to destroy the postal service's personnel system as a miscalculation. If the advancement of savings and remittance personnel depended on genuine talent and ability, and if their positions were fully guaranteed, then the bureau's staff would be aware that safeguarding the lifeline of the bureau was more important than individual gains. Would Liu and Yang have dared to engage in embezzlement without any fear? This is the second point we want to make. Regarding the two points above, the mistake of establishing a separate Savings and Remittance Bureau and the inappropriateness of the bureau's personnel recruitment have been repeatedly and vehemently conveyed to all sectors by our two postal workers' unions. We are not surprised by the discovery of the Liu-Yang embezzlement case this time, as it was expected. However, our two postal workers' unions have also taken preventive measures, proposing a plan to consolidate the postal base and launching a large-scale campaign to eliminate hidden dangers in advance. The biggest goal of the plan to consolidate the postal base proposed by our two postal workers' unions last year was to recover the Savings and Remittance Bureau and restore the previous state of postal personnel concurrently handling savings and remittance business. The plan has already been discussed by the Postal Economic System Research Committee for more than a year and has been recommended to the National Government, requesting its adoption and implementation. Unexpectedly, our government still has some reservations and has delayed the full implementation of the plan until now. This is what we are greatly puzzled by. Now, the Liu-Yang embezzlement case has been investigated by the Shanghai District Court and evidence has been found, and the Procuratorate has filed a public prosecution. Liu and Yang will naturally be punished by law. In addition to urging the judicial authorities to conduct a thorough investigation and severely punish them to restore the hard-earned money of the common people, we are more determined to realize the plan to consolidate the postal base and deeply feel the urgent need to implement the plan and continue to strive for it. We hope that people from all walks of life will pay attention to this case and to the postal savings and remittance business, which is related to the economy of all sectors, and give us a sympathetic response. It is fortunate for the nation and fortunate for our colleagues. Jointly issued by the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Shanghai Postal Workers' Association on October 25, 1933.

List of Emergency Relief Efforts Undertaken by the Joint International Famine Relief Commission 167

A record of the emergency relief efforts undertaken by the Joint International Famine Relief Commission: (Both Banks of the Yellow River) The commission believes that the number of flood victims is very large, and the weather is already cold, so there is an urgent need for clothing. 10,000 new cotton garments have been made and are being discussed with the National Government's Yellow River Flood Relief Committee to request free transportation. However, there is still concern that the clothing is insufficient for distribution, and it is planned to continue making 10,000 garments to make up the shortfall. (Chongming) The commission reports that the entire county has been severely affected by the disaster. More than 2,000 packages of white rice and corn, as well as 2,000 cotton garments, have been shipped successively. Special commissioners have been dispatched and are currently distributing the goods. However, there is still concern that the clothing and rice are insufficient, and it is planned to continue shipping them to avoid any feeling of being left out. (Qidong) The commission has allocated several hundred dan of rice, 2,500 garments, and 6,000 yuan in relief funds, and is currently conducting emergency relief efforts in conjunction with the Jisheng Society. (Chuansha) The commission has allocated 5,000 yuan and 1,000 cotton garments, and has also conducted emergency relief efforts in conjunction with the Jisheng Society. (Nanhui) The commission has publicly appointed Mr. Lu Bohong to carry 3,000 yuan to conduct on-site inspections and distributions. (Baoshan) The commission reports that the flood disaster in Changxing and other areas is severe, and food supplies have been cut off. It has immediately allocated several hundred dan of rice and 1,500 cotton garments and pants to Mr. Zhang Gongquan for transportation and relief. (Shaanxi) In addition to continuously transporting large quantities of relief grain and cash, purchasing seeds, and providing medicines, the commission has allocated another 40,000 yuan for post-disaster recovery to undertake the Jinghui No. 2 and No. 5 branch canal projects, and 20,000 yuan for well-digging projects. All the projects will be completed this month, it is said. (Gaoyou) During the floods of previous years, the six major breaches in the county, including the retaining wall for military grain, were repaired by the commission. Due to time and economic constraints, earthwork was used, but the cost was no less than 300,000 yuan. In order to ensure consolidation and prevent future disasters, the commission is now rebuilding the stone works and has reportedly raised tens of thousands of yuan, which will be used for construction next month, it is said. (Qingjiangpu) Located in Huai'an County, the Fu Gong Dam is dedicated to protecting the waters of Hongze, Baima, and Bao Ying, safeguarding 8,000 acres of farmland and the lives of 100,000 people. The dam collapsed during the floods of previous years, and the people were poor and unable to repair it. The commission joined forces with the Jiangsu Disaster Prevention Association to undertake the repair of the dam, which was completed long ago. The cost was reportedly nearly 30,000 yuan, it is said.

Recent News on the Mutual Aid and Cooperative Societies in the Yellow River Disaster Area; Shanghai Office of the Joint International Famine Relief Commission Decides to Establish Them 168

The Shanghai office of the China Joint International Famine Relief Commission, located on the second floor of the Central Building at No. 49 Nanjing Road, reports that due to the Yellow River overflowing its banks, breaching dikes, and flooding more than fifty counties in southern Hebei, central Henan, and western Shandong, rural buildings, farming implements, and seeds have been completely destroyed. About three million disaster victims lack clothing and food and are crying out for help. Although the Beijing headquarters is actively raising relief funds and carrying out emergency relief efforts in the disaster area, the fundamental solution is to restore rural organizations in order to ensure post-disaster recovery. It has been decided to gradually establish mutual aid societies and cooperative societies in the Yellow River disaster area and to send personnel to the disaster areas most severely affected to carry out this work. Using scientific methods, the spirit of the latest mutual aid societies and cooperative societies in the East and West will be adopted, and practical measures such as loans instead of direct relief will be implemented to meet the needs of disaster-stricken farmers to restore rural organizations and finance. Currently, Mr. An Xianjin, a foreign staff member, and Mr. Shen Mingsan, a Chinese staff member, are jointly raising relief funds from Chinese and foreign philanthropists and actively carrying out the plan in order to achieve its realization in the shortest possible time. This is truly good news for the Yellow River disaster victims.

Page 12

Forging Telegraphs to Damage the Reputation of Silk Firms; Xing Zhonghe Charged with Two Crimes 169

The annual production of yellow and white silk in Shandong Province is quite large. Most of these merchants personally transport their goods to Shanghai and hand them over to silk firms that specialize in selling yellow and white silk for consignment sales. Some, relying solely on the usual reputation of the silk firms, directly ship their goods to the silk firms for consignment sales. Some silk firms with strong capital even send their own staff to the production areas to purchase the goods themselves. For example, Hengsheng Gong in Hengyuan Lane on Tianjin Road, Yifengchang on Jiangxi Road, and Yonghecheng at No. 529 Tianjin Road all operate in the yellow and white silk business. Competition among firms has always been fierce, and the means of competition have been getting worse and worse, becoming exceptionally base. Recently, false information has been spread through telegraphs to damage the reputation of competitors. On July 31 of this year, someone attempted to harm Hengsheng Gong and Yifengchang by falsely using the name of Wang Shuchang at No. 98 Bafang Lane in the Eight Immortals Bridge area to send a telegram to the Shandong Qingzhou Linqu Silk Industry Protection Committee, stating that Hengyi and Yifeng owe banks too much money and that it has been decided to seize their goods for compensation, or to auction them off to make up for the shortfall, and to sue them for any remaining amount. Ten such telegrams were sent at the same time. In addition to the Silk Industry Protection Committee, various merchants operating in yellow and white silk in various places, including Yongjude, Jutongxing, Hengshunxing, Fuhetai, Delong, Yuanfeng, Shenji, Fucheng, Guangzengmao, and others in Zhoucun and Zhoufang, received these telegrams and did not dare to continue entrusting the two firms with consignment sales. At this time, Yonghecheng took the opportunity to solicit business from merchants in various places. Subsequently, after the staff of Hengsheng Gong and Yifengchang stationed in Shandong inquired with the Silk Industry Protection Committee about the reason why various merchants had stopped entrusting them with the sale of goods, they were able to read the above-mentioned telegram. It was then notified to the Shanghai firms that the false telegram was actually fabricated by Xing Zhonghe (also known as Xing Zhonghe), the manager of Yonghecheng Silk Firm. Xing's action was partly to compete for business and partly to vent his anger and seek revenge. Previously, when Xing was the manager of Yuhecheng Silk Firm, Yuhecheng and several affiliated firms, including Yutaixing, Yuxingcheng, Yucheng, Yongxiecheng, Yongfukang, Wufutang, Xinji, and Yitaicheng, owed Hengsheng Gong and Yifengchang a total of more than 300,000 yuan. Cai and Zhang repeatedly urged Xing to repay the debt, which inevitably caused resentment in his heart. Therefore, he took the opportunity to retaliate, believing that there was no better plan than to harm others and benefit himself. After Cai and Zhang clarified the matter, they hired lawyers Cai Liucheng and Sun Yuan to file a criminal lawsuit against Xing, accusing him of spreading rumors and using forged documents, and demanding severe punishment. The First Special District Court has held two hearings on the case, but no verdict has been reached. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui continued the trial, but the most important witnesses, such as the staff of the telegraph bureau's reception and dispatch department, and the person who drafted the telegraph draft at the defendant's silk firm, did not appear in court, so important facts could not be reliably proven, and it was difficult to proceed with the trial. Judge Liu ordered a postponement of the case and a summons for the witnesses to be questioned again.

Bureau of Weights and Measures Notifies that Prices Should be Marked in the New System 170

The Shanghai Bureau of Weights and Measures sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating that: "We have received instruction No. 5278 from the National Bureau of Weights and Measures of the Ministry of Industry, which states that the conversion of prices is crucial to the promotion of the new system. Now that the country is universally unified, the recording of various price quantities should be marked according to the new system, such as 'per city stone,' 'city dan,' 'city catty,' 'city tael,' 'metric ton,' and other units, so as to deeply penetrate the public and ensure compliance. Recently, we have found that economic news published in newspapers in various places does not mark the units of 'stone' and 'dan' for various goods. It is not clear whether the new system has been changed or whether the old system is still being used, which is easily misunderstood. We hereby order the said bureau to comply immediately, contact the local chamber of commerce and trade associations, and make earnest corrections to benefit the people's livelihood." In accordance with this order, we should comply and send a letter for your reference, and request you to instruct your affiliated trade associations to comply accordingly. In the future, the recording of various price quantities in the economic news of newspapers in our city should be marked according to the new system, such as "per city stone," "city dan," "city catty," "city tael," "metric ton," and other units, so as to show unification and benefit the people's livelihood. It is sincerely public friendship, it said. It is heard that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has transferred the letter to the various trade associations for compliance.

Municipal Government Strictly Prohibits Unauthorized Issuance of Lottery Tickets 171

Recently, some companies and stores in this city have been issuing lottery tickets without authorization. Although the government has repeatedly prohibited this, some have still failed to comply. The Municipal Government specifically issued a notice yesterday strictly prohibiting this. The text is recorded as follows: "Issuing lottery tickets without government approval is a violation of criminal law. Furthermore, collecting money and using lotteries to allow people to gain profit by chance has long been prohibited. However, recently, various companies and stores in this city have been cleverly devising names and issuing lottery tickets or similar things without authorization. Such rampant speculation and its extreme harm are beyond imagination. All lottery tickets and similar methods that have not been approved by the government should be strictly prohibited, and they should not be advertised in newspapers to prevent malpractice. We hereby issue this notice for general knowledge, and everyone must abide by it without fail. Sincerely, this notice."

Cha Ruilong Accused of Embezzling Inheritance; Inquiry Against Cha Ruanyun Unsuccessful, Hearing Rescheduled 173

Cha Ruilong, a strongman who is currently a shareholder and director of the China Film Company, was recently sued in the First Special District Court by his cousin, Cha Ruiyun, through lawyers Zhu Sifu, Yang Ruinian, and Li Mian, on criminal charges of embezzling inheritance. The facts of the lawsuit are as follows: The plaintiff's father, De Cun, and Cha Ruilong's father, De Yuan, were brothers with the same parents. They owned ancestral land worth more than 100,000 yuan. Because De Yuan and De Cun were close brothers, they never divided the property. De Yuan managed it, and they were harmonious and had no disputes. In 1917, De Cun died of illness, leaving behind a five-year-old son, Rui Lian. In less than four years, Rui Lian's mother also passed away, so De Yuan raised Rui Lian. Not long after, De Yuan and his wife passed away one after another. All the property of both families was managed by Ruilong. At that time, Ruilian was not yet an adult and was still studying. Unexpectedly, Ruilong was stingy with tuition fees and ordered him to learn typesetting. Rui Lian did not want to, so he was instead ordered to work as a waiter at the National Hotel to support himself. He did not give any of the property that his cousin should have received. Rui Lian was still young and did not dispute this. It was not until the year before last that Cha Ruilong's sister, Xin Yuan, sued the district court because her brother did not divide the inheritance. As a result, more than 50,000 yuan of De Yuan's inheritance was fully divided and it was stated that the remaining 50,000 yuan of inheritance was under De Cun's name, so it could not be divided. Now that Rui Lian is older, he has repeatedly demanded that Ruilong return the inheritance, but has been refused. Rui Lian believes that Ruilong is actually embezzling the inheritance, so he filed a lawsuit, requesting that he be punished according to Article 356 of the Criminal Law. The First Special District Court held a hearing on this case yesterday afternoon. Cha Ruilong was not found after investigation, so the plaintiff's representative, lawyer Yang Ruinian, stated that the defendant's address was initially unclear, but it has now been found that he lives at No. 1105 behind the Jinsidu Temple on Kangnuot Road. The court stated that the defendant had not been summoned, so it was difficult to proceed, and ordered that the case be rescheduled so that the plaintiff could summon the defendant to court for further verification.

On the morning of the day before yesterday, at around 9 AM, a customer suddenly came to Ruichangxiang Leather Goods Store at No. 45 Jiuxiaochang in Xinbeimen and used Feng Xianming (nine years old), the son of a Shaoxing woman, Feng Chen, who lived at No. 223 Xueyuan Road, to swindle two pieces of sheepskin, worth more than 50 yuan, and then escaped without a trace. The customer selected twelve of them (priced at more than 30 yuan). Later, he claimed that these gray squirrels had to be taken home for his parents to see before he could make a decision, but since they did not know each other, he asked his nephew (referring to the child he brought) to wait in the store for a while and he would be back soon. The store did not suspect anything because he wanted to take the goods to see and left his nephew in the store to wait, so he let the customer take them away. I met him on the way, and he bought me many pieces of milk candy, gave them to me, and brought me here to play. Now I want to go home, etc. Only then did the store realize that it had been deceived, so it called the police on duty and took the child to the Second Division of the First District for questioning. Then, at around 10 PM, Dai Wenhua, an employee of Ruichangxiang Leather Goods Store, and Sun Shizhen, an employee of Hengchangxiang Leather Goods Store at No. 128 Jiuxiaochang, went out on business and happened to see the teenager who had swindled the sheepskin walking near Xinbeimen. Sun Shizhen, an employee of Hengchangxiang Leather Goods Store, also stated that the store had previously been swindled of a piece of sheepskin by the same method. Then, Li Caibao, the local owner of Lifuxing Leather Shoe Store at No. 364 Fangbang Road, filed a case, identifying the teenager as having come to the store at around 11 AM on the 20th of this month and swindled two pairs of leather shoes. When questioned, the teenager claimed his name was Shi Zhidong, he was eighteen years old, from Chongming, and lived at No. 36 Xueyuan Road. He used to be a painter in Qingyunge at No. 104 Jiuxiaochang, specializing in painting various types of Chinese paintings. He is now unemployed and has difficulty making a living, so he had no choice but to resort to this strategy. All the goods he swindled have been pawned and used, he said. Considering that the person has swindled goods from other stores, it is decided that it is not limited to Ruichangxiang Leather Goods Store and several other stores. Chinese and Foreign Pharmacy Drug Case Involves Zhang Wanrong: Zhang Claims His Real Name is Wanrong, Used Zhang Surname to Change Certificate: Court Still Needs to Investigate 179

The Chinese and Foreign Pharmacy at No. 69 Guangdong Road was previously searched by the competent police force on May 10, 1931 for privately selling morphine. A large amount of drugs were found in the pharmacy, and the store owner, Qiao Ziyun from Datuan, Pudong, was arrested. After a final trial by the First Special District Local Court, the defendants were sentenced to imprisonment and the drugs were destroyed. However, a land business license was found at the time of the search, which was filled in under the name of Zhang Wanrong. No one claimed it until the case was closed, so it was temporarily attached to the file. Later, someone claiming to be Zhang Wanrong hired a lawyer to apply for the return of the certificate, but the court at that time still retained the certificate because Qiao Ziyun's fine had not been paid. Now that Qiao has been released from prison and other procedures have been completed, the person claiming to be Zhang Wanrong has hired a lawyer to apply again. The judge of the execution court discovered, after reviewing the file, that Qiao Ziyun had stated during the court hearing that his accomplice Zhang Changgui was Zhang Wanrong. The judge in charge of the Qiao case issued an arrest warrant for Zhang, as he was on the run. Now that the suspect dares to come forward, he should be investigated strictly. The address was checked according to his statement and the competent police force was notified to send detectives to Rongchangxiang Watch Store at No. 190 Fujian Road to arrest Zhang Wanrong and to verify that the watch store was opened by Zhang. In addition to running this business, he also serves as a compradore for the Japanese Hattori Trading Company. He is exceptionally respectful to the Japanese owner on weekdays and is deeply trusted by the employer. He has been in the position for more than 20 years, so his family has also become wealthy. Yesterday, he was escorted to the First Special Court by the police force. After Court President Qian Hongye questioned him, the police lawyer Ru Baoyi explained the case and requested that Zhang be temporarily detained, as the police force still needed to investigate everything. Zhang Wanrong hired a lawyer to defend himself, saying that his real name was Wanrong, not Zhang Wanrong. The reason why he called himself Zhang Wanrong was that he partnered with Zhang Changgui in the real estate business that year and bought a piece of land. When he went to the Land Bureau to change the business license, he used Changgui's surname and Wanrong's name to form the three characters "Zhang Wanrong" and filled it in the certificate as the account name. Therefore, he applied for the return of the business license under the name of Zhang Wanrong this time. Qiao Ziyun's statement that his accomplice Zhang Wanrong must be someone else, etc. Judge Qian questioned Zhang himself, and he made the same statement. The court believed that it was necessary to conduct a detailed investigation to determine whether it was a pretext or sophistry. Zhang Wanrong was ordered to pay a bail of 3,000 yuan for a rescheduled hearing.

Japanese Ship Collides With and Damages Large Sand Ship 180

Ju Shoubai from Jingjiang owns a four-masted large sand ship, which is used to transport piglets and miscellaneous goods from his hometown to various ports for sale. On the 11th of this month, he loaded 156 piglets and dozens of packages of peanuts from his hometown and sailed to Ningbo for sale under the supervision of Du Yusheng and ten other crew members. At 3 AM on the 13th, when sailing to the sea off Chuansha shoal, about 40 to 50 miles outside Wusongkou, it was dark when the Japanese Mitsui & Co.'s coal ship Katsuragiyama Maru came head-on and sailed in at high speed. The Ju ship tried to avoid it urgently, but the ship was moving too fast and was violently struck on the stern. The ship was completely shattered, especially the fifth cabin, which suffered the most damage. The entire cabin was flooded, and most of the piglets drowned. Du Dada fractured his knee. The ship was about to sink. After causing the accident, the ship dropped anchor and inspected the Ju ship, ordering the crew to find a way to force the ship to the shoal and saying that the matter would be resolved after arriving in Shanghai. After speaking, it weighed anchor and sailed to Shanghai, berthing at the Huatong Wharf in Pudong to unload its cargo. After the accident, ten people were left to guard the ship. Crew member Xiang Yousheng returned to his hometown alone and came to Shanghai yesterday with shipowner Ju Shoubai to claim compensation.

Ningbo Fellow Townsmen's Association Sends Letter to Assist in the Case of Chen Zhanglin's Tragic Death: Letter Sent to the Public Works Bureau Yesterday to Uphold Justice 183

Chen Zhanglin, an employee of Erwo Leather Gloves Company, went out to buy goods on the 22nd of this month. While passing through the area of Wenzhiji Si Tuolu on Suzhou Road, he was struck by falling wood from the Dachang Construction Factory, which hit Chen Zhanglin on the head. He was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment but died the next day. The company believes that Dachang Factory was negligent and should be held responsible for negligent homicide. Yesterday, a letter was sent to the Ningbo Fellow Townsmen's Association in Shanghai to request assistance. The reporter of Heping News Agency learned that the Association had transferred the letter to the Public Works Bureau, requesting it to uphold justice and initiate a public prosecution. The original letter is recorded below: Dear Sirs, According to a letter from Erwo Leather Gloves Company, our company's employee Chen Zhanglin, a native of Jiangshan, Ningbo, aged 29, went out to buy goods at about 2 PM on October 22nd of the lunar calendar. More than ten minutes later, a neighbor came to report that Chen Zhanglin had been struck on the head by falling wood from the Dachang Construction Factory building the Bank of China on Suzhou Road, resulting in brain matter flowing out. The Chinese police officer No. 304 and special patrol officer immediately called Renji Hospital and ordered an ambulance to take him to the hospital for treatment. He died of his injuries on the morning of the 23rd. Upon investigation, the cause was that the newly built bamboo fence of the Dachang Construction Factory was not secure, resulting in the tragedy. The Public Works Bureau stipulates that bamboo fences must be erected for building construction to protect the public from danger. Now the factory's fence was not secure and caused the disaster, which is a violation of the Public Works Bureau's regulations and cannot be held without due responsibility. Chen Zhanglin's death, although not intentional murder by Dachang Factory, is undoubtedly negligent homicide. Since the factory has committed a criminal offense, the Public Works Bureau should be requested to initiate a public prosecution to maintain the law and to ensure the safety and tranquility of the public in the future. Therefore, we especially ask your association to forward a letter to the Public Works Bureau, requesting it to deal with Dachang Construction Factory strictly. Fortunately, do not neglect it. However, Chen Zhanglin has a senile mother above, a young and weak wife in the middle, and young children below. The family relies on his life. How can we take care of his descendants? The situation is tragic and pitiful, etc. Chen Zhanglin suffered a tragic misfortune, which was indeed caused by the insecure fence. The Dachang Factory cannot shirk its responsibility. According to the foregoing circumstances, it is requested that your Public Works Bureau examine and verify the facts, uphold justice, and initiate a public prosecution to avenge the deceased and rely on the living. We hope that this request can be honored (Heping News Agency).

(12) Requesting the alma mater to completely abolish the salaries of non-incumbent faculty and staff.

Case of Giant Wood Falling and Killing a Pedestrian Opens for Trial This Afternoon: Jiatai Tea Shop Employee Has Already Confessed: Plaintiff Asks for More Than 50,000 Yuan in Compensation 187

Chen Ronggui (38 years old), an employee of the textile department of the German Miye Foreign Company at No. 16 Guangdong Road in the Public Concession, lived at No. 126 Jiuxiaochang in Xinbeimen. It was his habit to leave early and return late every day. Chen's wife, Huang (40 years old), had two sons and five daughters, and their lives were still warm and full. Unexpectedly, at 5 PM on May 12th of this year, while returning home from the company, while passing in front of the Lao Jiatai Tea Shop at No. 46 Lao Beimen Street in the French Concession, a giant piece of wood, more than ten feet long, fell from the roof of the shop, striking him on the head. He became dizzy and fell to the ground. A nearby Chinese police officer found him and took Chen to the police station, which transferred him to Renji Hospital for treatment. He died of his injuries. The court verified the incident and summoned the tea shop's employees to the scene, who admitted that the wood did fall from the roof of the shop. Later, the deceased's mother, Chen Zhang (67 years old), and wife, Chen Huang, hired lawyers Shen Yi, Wang Jianfan, and Lu Hongyi to file a private prosecution with the Second Special District Court, accusing Pan Jucai and others of the tea shop of causing death due to negligence, requesting that they be punished according to the law, and filing an accompanying civil suit, requesting that they be ordered to compensate all losses. The court judges repeatedly summoned the plaintiff and defendant to the case for questioning and instructed both parties to try to reach a settlement, but it did not succeed. Unexpectedly, the second plaintiff, Chen Huang, fell ill due to depression because of her husband's tragic death and died on the seventh day of the eighth month of the lunar calendar. It is now known that Chen's family has left behind an old mother and seven children, as well as an unmarried sister of the deceased (51 years old). In order to provide food for the living and comfort the spirits of the dead, they have hired lawyer Zhu Gaorong to request the court to uphold justice, order the defendant to compensate all losses of more than 50,000 yuan, and maintain the lives of the nine members of the family. After the court received the complaint, it scheduled a hearing at 1:30 PM today to summon the plaintiff and defendant to the case for trial (Guomin News Agency).

Rice Boat Robbed - Sheng Jintao Cleaned Out - Rural Boatmen's Conversation Causes Disaster 188

Recently, Sheng Jintao's rice boat loaded 200 dan of white rice from the Yi Sheng Xiang firm in Jiahu, to be transported to Shanghai for sale by a rice merchant named Lu. Due to market conditions, the firm urged Sheng's boat to travel quickly, so as to arrive in Shanghai early for sale. However, on the afternoon before yesterday, when sailing to the 18-li-long Pu surface of the Nanhuangpu, it was getting late. Sheng, seeing that the Pu surface had many bends and would be difficult to navigate at night, noticed several cargo boats heading south anchored there for the night. Therefore, he also sailed to the Pu bank and anchored. He further saw a rural boat anchored in front of Sheng's boat, only a few feet away, outside the cargo boats staying overnight. Sheng didn't suspect anything, and the crew members chatted with the people on the rural boat. Unexpectedly, when dawn broke yesterday morning, all the cargo boats that had stayed overnight there had already sailed away. Sheng instructed the crew to get up and prepare to sail, but they saw four or five people on the shore running down to the rural boat, which immediately sailed to the side of Sheng's boat. Seven or eight people jumped aboard, threatened the boatmen with guns, preventing them from making noise, and drove all the crew members into the cabin. They asked who the boat owner was, but the crew didn't answer and were beaten with sticks. Sheng knew they were robbers and said, "Our boat is carrying passengers and goods, and we only take the water fare. The goods must be delivered to Shanghai. You can take the money." He handed over ten yuan in cash he had in his pocket, but the robbers didn't believe him and searched everywhere. They smashed open a suitcase and robbed seventy or eighty yuan. The robbers thought Sheng was unusually cunning, dragged him out and beat him severely, demanding that he quickly hand over any hidden silver. Sheng told them that he had no other silver hidden anywhere. Then, another small boat came. The robbers opened the cabin and began to move the rice into the two small boats. When they were full and could not hold any more, the robbers stopped. The robbers jumped onto the two small boats, fired a shot into the air as they left, and then sped east towards Pudong. After the robbers left, the crew members came out of the cabin and saw that Sheng was seriously injured. Sheng was from Shenglonghua Shengqiao, so they sailed the boat to Shengqiao and sent Sheng home, where he was treated by a doctor. More than ten shi of rice were robbed. In the afternoon, the crew informed rice merchant Lu, requesting that the authorities be notified to arrest the robbers and recover the stolen goods.

Lin Yaoxuan Encounters a "Honey Trap" - Case Adjourned for Retrial 189

Lin Yaoxuan from Sichuan, who runs a white fungus and foreign goods business in Shanghai, was introduced by Hu Ruiting, a foreign goods broker he knew, to Shen Wu, the wife of Shen Shou Kang, the owner of the Jiankang Hospital at 25 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, and had a secret affair. They had trysts several times in rooms at the Zhongnan and Dahu hotels. On the afternoon of the 29th of last month at 2 p.m., Hu arranged for Lin and Shen to meet at the Central Hotel in room 523 for another liaison. As soon as Lin and Shen entered the room, Hu made an excuse to leave, colluding with Shen Shou Kang, Chen Fuliang, Li Hong, and three or four others to rush to the Central Hotel and extort money from Lin. They then kidnapped Lin to the law office of Zhang Wei on Avenue Edward VII, forcing him to write two IOU notes for 500 yuan each and taking his watch and cash before releasing him. Lin believed that Hu, Chen, and the others had deliberately set up a "honey trap" to extort money, so he reported it to the French police. The detectives arrested Chen Fuliang, Li Hong, and Hu Ruiting, and retrieved the IOU notes and watch as evidence, sending them to the Second Special Court for interrogation and detention. Later, Shen Shou Kang and his wife, knowing they could not evade responsibility, surrendered to the police and were sent to the court for prosecution. Judge Zhang Chaozuo repeatedly held court sessions to try the cases together. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday morning, another hearing was held. At noon, Judge Zhang summoned witnesses in Criminal Court No. 1 for questioning. Liu Jingcai, a waiter from the Zhongnan Hotel, and Xu Yiming, a waiter from the Central Hotel, brought the circular ledger to testify about Lin Yaoxuan's entering rooms with Shen and Hu. After questioning both the plaintiffs and defendants, as it was past 1 p.m., the court adjourned the hearing to be rescheduled. The defendants were returned to custody separately.

Sino-Foreign Relief Association to Establish Rural Cooperatives in Yellow River Disaster Area - 20,000 Cotton-Padded Coats for Yellow River Victims Departed Last Night 191

The Shanghai office of the China Sino-Foreign Relief Association believes that the Yellow River's overflowing and breaching of dikes has submerged over fifty counties in southern Hebei, eastern Henan, and western Shandong. Rural buildings, farming tools, and seeds have been completely destroyed, leaving three million victims without food or clothing, urgently in need of aid. Although the National Government's Yellow River Disaster Relief Committee, various charitable organizations, and the Association's Beijing headquarters have actively raised funds and provided emergency relief in the disaster areas, the fundamental solution is to restore rural organization. It has been decided to establish rural mutual aid societies and cooperatives in the Yellow River disaster areas in stages, sending personnel to the most severely affected areas to handle the matter on the ground, in order to restore rural organization and finance. Currently, Mr. An Xianjin (English), a British executive, and Mr. Shen Mingsan, a Chinese executive, are working together to actively raise relief funds from Chinese and foreign philanthropists, with the aim of implementing this plan in the shortest possible time. Furthermore, the Disaster Relief Group of the National Government's Yellow River Water Disaster Relief Committee has purchased 100,000 sets of cotton-padded clothing for distribution. The first batch of 20,000 sets was shipped to the disaster areas of Hebei, Henan, and Shandong provinces on the 15th for distribution. The second batch of 20,000 sets has also been delivered and departed last night.

Mr. and Mrs. Haiberg Depart Shanghai for India 193

The German Haiberg Circus will be performing in India in a few weeks. Mr. Haiberg, the head of the troupe, and his wife, are scheduled to depart for India today to make preliminary arrangements. Mr. Haiberg, who has traveled the world, felt particularly attached to China during his stay in Shanghai for about twenty days. He was extremely busy with social engagements, making new acquaintances and renewing old friendships. Before leaving, he told reporters that he had traveled the world with his circus troupe, but he felt particularly attached to China. He added that the Chinese and foreign residents of Shanghai had shown great kindness and support to the circus troupe, making the performances very popular. He was deeply grateful for this kindness and hoped to return in the future with even grander and more advanced performances.

Before Mr. Haiberg left Shanghai, he sent several representatives to various parts of China to collect various rare and exotic birds and animals, making the menagerie even more complete. All troupe affairs during the remaining performance period in Shanghai will be managed by the general manager, Mr. Schaevitz.

Haiberg and his circus have been performing in Shanghai for some time, and the history of his childhood is of great interest to us. Even as a child, he was exceptionally brave. At the age of thirteen, he once entered a cage containing no fewer than twenty kinds of ferocious beasts, such as lions and tigers. His father, catching sight of this, rushed to pull him out, and thereafter forbade him from mingling with the animals to prevent danger. His father was a great circus owner and later sent someone to India to buy animals. Haiberg accompanied him, marking his first trip to India. Later, this person fell ill, so the young and inexperienced Haiberg had to take full responsibility for the transport. There were twelve elephants, four hundred monkeys, three hundred snakes, and many other birds and animals, all to be transported to Germany, which was no easy task. Later, Haiberg went alone to Africa to buy five hundred ostriches, which were crammed into a small boat. The suffering of crowding and filth is hard to imagine, but he remained calm. Crossing the Cape of Good Hope, a great storm made progress even more difficult. The voyage took a total of thirty-nine days to reach its destination on the way home. Such was the hardship of the work. Now that we see his magnificent menagerie and observe his decisiveness in handling affairs as a child, we know that his success is not without cause. Since the Haiberg Circus began performing in Shanghai, the people of Shanghai have been amazed by the spectacle and marveled at his incredible animal training techniques. Now, for the sake of increasing the knowledge of circus enthusiasts, the "Chen Bao" and the Chinese Art and Science Society have specially invited Mr. Schaevitz, the manager of the Haiberg Circus, and Mr. Haiberg's son, Herbert Haiberg, to give a public lecture in the auditorium of the Chinese Art and Science Society at No. 45 Avenue Amiral Foch on October 26th (today) at 3:30 p.m., with the topic "How to Train Various Animals". Mr. Schaevitz has been the general manager of the troupe for forty-five years and is very familiar with the situation in various countries. During the lecture, he will reveal all the secrets of training, which will surely be welcomed by the general audience. Starting at 4 p.m., the Educational Film Association will also screen films at the Chinese Art and Science Society, including educational, industrial, and humorous films, which will further increase the interest of the audience.

Investigation Report on the Qidong Disaster 196

The Chinese Jisheng Society and the Sino-Foreign Relief Association jointly organized emergency relief for the Qidong disaster, publicly recommending members Qiu and Lu as the director and deputy director, along with relief workers, to go and investigate the disaster. According to the report received after they left, on the 18th of this month, Director Zhang Shunru of the Education Bureau accompanied them to Jiangxia Village, District 8, as the starting point of the disaster area in the southeast. The area is known for producing cotton. After two hurricanes, seawater surged in, with the water level being over ten feet high outside the embankment and four, five, six, or seven feet high inside the embankment. As a result, the seawater soaked cotton fields and cotton stalks, resulting in absolutely no harvest. At that time, one or two hundred people were swept away by the seawater, with no trace of their bodies. There are names and corpses for more than 380 others. Grass huts within the outer embankment have been completely washed away, with no rice, no clothes, and no homes. They are begging for food in the inland areas. Those who are stronger are either helping with work or seeking help from relatives and friends to make a living. Due to the soil being exposed to saltwater, they have no hope of planting anything next year. The local authorities are discussing post-disaster relief measures, but the only way is to rebuild the outer embankment, using labor as relief, widening and raising it based on the old foundation, about nine thousand feet or more. However, this requires a huge amount of money, which is planned to be collected from local land taxes from the owners. There is still a shortfall, and they are requesting the Shanghai charitable organizations to provide assistance. If this embankment is successful, future disasters can be prevented. However, the Jiang embankment is not included. The local authorities are surveying and estimating these two engineering plans after measuring, and are actively carrying them out with the efforts of everyone. However, there are currently forty to fifty thousand disaster victims waiting to be fed, and the Association's relief funds are insufficient for distribution. It is hoped that more funds will be raised to provide relief. It is said that the Association first loaded 1,700 shi of Xian rice and 2,500 sets of new cotton clothing and transported them to the disaster area for distribution, but it is like a drop in the bucket and will not solve the problem. It is hoped that philanthropists at home and abroad will generously donate to save lives.

French Municipal Council Cemetery Regulations 198

The following is a record of the regulations for the management of the Xujiahui Road Cemetery by the French Municipal Council, promulgated by the French Consul General in Shanghai: (Article 1) The cemetery shall be open to the public from 7 a.m. to 7 p.m. from May 1st to September 30th each year, and from 8 a.m. to 5 p.m. from October 1st to April 30th. (Article 2) No vehicles, except for hearses, shall be allowed to enter the cemetery. (Article 3) Children under the age of twelve shall only be allowed to enter under adult supervision. (Article 4) Dogs, even if held on a leash, shall not be allowed to enter. (Article 5) Anyone wishing to take photographs or film in the cemetery must first obtain written approval from the Municipal Administration of the Municipal Council. (Article 6) Music is not allowed in the cemetery. (Article 7) Anyone wishing to erect a tombstone must first apply to the Engineering Department of the Municipal Council for a construction permit. Anyone wishing to move, alter, or repair a tombstone must also first obtain a permit. The permit shall be given to the gravedigger for inspection during the execution of the project. Tombstones shall only be erected four months after burial. (Article 8) The area of each tomb is stipulated to be two meters by eight decimeters. The tombstone and surrounding decorations shall not exceed the stipulated area under any circumstances. No benches, awnings, or shelters shall be erected on the tomb. (Article 9) If the tombstone or surrounding decorations are damaged, the family shall repair or remove them. (Article 10) The Municipal Council reserves the right to remove all broken sacrificial utensils, withered flowers, debris, and damaged tombstones. (Article 11) The Municipal Council's staff shall not be responsible for the maintenance of graves under any circumstances. (Article 12) The work of tidying up graves shall be carried out from 8:30 a.m. to 11:30 a.m. and from 1 p.m. to 5 p.m. daily. No work shall be carried out on Sundays and holidays. (Article 13) The Municipal Council shall not be responsible for any damage to tombstones and surrounding decorations, flower pots, or loss of funeral decorations. (Article 14) Planting trees on graves is strictly prohibited, but small plants may be planted within the area stipulated in Article 8. The Municipal Council reserves the right to remove or prune any plants that extend beyond the boundary of the tomb. (Article 15) The corpse to be buried shall be firmly placed in a coffin before being transported into the cemetery. (Article 16) No burial or exhumation shall be allowed without the express order of the Municipal Council. No burial or exhumation shall be allowed after 5 p.m. from May 1st to September 30th each year, and after 4:30 p.m. from October 1st to April 30th. (Article 17) Anyone who violates these regulations shall be punished in accordance with Article 5 of the regulations of the Health and Relief Department.

Educational News from Other Places

Important Resolutions of the Ministry of Education's Vocational Education Design Committee (Part 1) 205

In October of this year, the Ministry of Education compiled vocational education laws, which are divided into the following: 1. The educational objectives of the Republic of China and their implementation guidelines; 2. Methods for determining the trend of educational implementation; 3. Proposals for determining the trend of educational facilities; 4. A general order to all provinces and cities to restrict the establishment of ordinary middle schools and increase the establishment of vocational schools, adding vocational departments or vocational subjects to ordinary middle schools, and requiring county junior middle schools to establish or transform into rural normal schools and vocational departments; 5. Implementation plans for establishing secondary agricultural and industrial schools in various provinces and cities; 6. Vocational School Law; 7. Vocational School Regulations, Vocational Supplementary School Regulations; 9. Outlines of methods for education administrative organs and primary and secondary schools in various provinces and cities to implement guidance on further education and careers; 10. Methods for setting up standards for the establishment and funding allocation of secondary schools in various provinces and cities; 11. Procedures for promoting vocational education in various provinces and cities; 12. Methods for registering, examining, and training vocational school teachers in various provinces and cities; 13. Outlines of teaching subjects and hours for each discipline in vocational schools, which have been announced separately by the government and the ministry. However, 14. Resolutions of the Ministry of Education's Vocational Education Design Committee, which are divided into three items: "Principles of Vocational School Facilities," "Standards of Vocational School Facilities," and "Standards of Vocational School Student Internships," are quite important and have not been disclosed in detail. It is worthwhile to publish them as a supplement. The details are recorded below:

▲Principles of Vocational School Facilities 206

(A) Regarding establishment: 1. Local education administrative organs should base the establishment of vocational schools at all levels on adapting to social needs and ensuring that students have adequate career prospects. 2. Before establishing vocational schools at all levels, local education administrative organs should conduct detailed surveys of social conditions and determine the standards for setting up school subjects. 3. Before establishing vocational schools at all levels, they should consult with local industrial organizations or establish them jointly. 4. Before establishing vocational schools at all levels, there should be detailed and concrete plans, as well as predicted future effects. 5. Education administrative organs should emphasize the actual effectiveness of vocational school expansion, not the exaggeration of quantity.

(B) Regarding equipment and funding: 1. Vocational schools at all levels must have substantial equipment and places for practice, so the start-up costs must be sufficient. 2. The places for practice in vocational schools at all levels must be able to accommodate all students for practice. 3. The recurring expenses of vocational schools at all levels should be limited to the most economical extent possible within the scope. The annual recurring expenses for a single-subject, single-grade should be based on an increase of 50% for provincial junior or senior middle schools in the local area as a principle. 4. The recurring expenses of vocational schools at all levels must have preparations for gradual expansion each year. (C) Regarding teachers: 1. Vocational school teachers must have extremely rich experience in specialized techniques. If there are no qualified teachers, technicians with rich experience and ordinary teachers will jointly teach. 2. Vocational school teachers must first demonstrate work and work with students, and then provide practical guidance. 3. The teaching methods of vocational school teachers must have concrete plans and determine the expected goals.

▲(D) Regarding students: (1) The aspirations of vocational school students should be based on serving in the vocational industry after graduation. (2) The age and qualifications of vocational school students should be slightly broader than the entrance qualifications for ordinary schools. (3) The graduation years of vocational school students must be very flexible, and being able to directly serve in the vocational industry should be the graduation standard.

▲(E) Regarding academic subjects, practice, and training: (1) The training of vocational school students should emphasize character cultivation, physical training, and vocational training equally, and special attention should be paid to character cultivation. (2) The working environment in which vocational students receive training should be consistent with the actual working environment in the future. (3) Vocational school students must strive to develop their ability to develop automatically. (4) Vocational school subjects are divided into general subjects, vocational subjects, and practice, and practice time must account for at least half of the total time. (5) Vocational school student practice materials, in addition to practicing basic work, should practice materials with commodity value, but excessive repetition should be avoided as much as possible, and the principle of manual work first and then machinery should be followed. (6) The products of vocational school student practice should be compared with social commodities to determine their advantages and disadvantages.

▲Standards for Vocational School Facilities ▲1. Types of Vocational Schools 207

The types of vocational schools vary from country to country around the world due to different social conditions and habits within the country. There are no clear regulations in our country regarding the types and scope of vocational schools, so those who run vocational schools have no basis to follow. The following are specially formulated:

(A) Scope: (1) The scope of establishing vocational schools can be divided into junior and senior levels according to the provisions of the Vocational School Law. (1) Junior vocational schools enroll primary school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications, and the length of study is one to three years, which may be shortened as necessary. (2) Senior vocational schools (1) enroll junior high school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications, and the length of study is three years. (2) Enroll primary school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications, and the length of study is five or six years.

(B) Types and names: (1) Junior vocational schools: (1) A school with only one vocational department is called a junior vocational school of a certain department. (2) A school with two vocational departments is called a junior vocational school of two certain departments. (3) A school with two or more agricultural, industrial, or commercial departments is called a junior agricultural, industrial, or commercial vocational school. (4) A school with several industries is called a junior vocational school. (2) Senior vocational schools: (1) A school with a single department is called a senior vocational school of a certain department. (2) A school with two departments is called a senior vocational school of two certain departments. (3) A school with two or more agricultural, industrial, or commercial departments is called a senior agricultural, industrial, or commercial vocational school. (4) A school with several industries is called a senior vocational school. (5) A school with both junior and senior levels is called a vocational school.

(C) Establishment and purpose: (1) Junior vocational schools: (1) Establishment should be based on counties and cities, but may also be established jointly by two or more counties or by private groups depending on the special circumstances of the region. (2) Purpose: (A) Junior agricultural science aims to cultivate farmers with general agricultural knowledge, so that they have the skills to operate independently, and can assist ordinary farmers to improve agriculture and rural areas. (B) Junior industrial science aims to cultivate skilled workers with general industrial knowledge and skills, so that they are knowledgeable workers in factories, and impart skills for independent living. (C) Junior commercial science aims to cultivate service personnel in ordinary commercial organizations and cultivate their ability to independently operate simple businesses. (3) Departments: (A) Agricultural science, such as general agriculture (rice, wheat, cotton, etc.), sericulture, forestry, animal husbandry, aquaculture, horticulture, etc. (B) Industrial science, such as rattan and bamboo work, carpentry, sheet metal work, electroplating, simple mechanical work, electrical engineering, electrical appliance installation and repair, watch repair, photography, printing, drawing, dyeing and weaving, silk weaving, cotton weaving, wool weaving, ceramics, simple chemical industry, etc., and may be merged or divided as appropriate according to local needs. (C) Commercial science, such as general commerce, bookkeeping, accounting, typing, advertising, etc. (D) Home economics, such as cooking, washing, flower making, sewing, embroidery, hairdressing, childcare, domestic work, etc. (E) Regarding other occupations, they should be established as appropriate according to local needs. (2) Senior vocational schools: (1) Establishment should be based on the province or the municipality directly under the Executive Yuan, but may also be established by counties and cities or private groups depending on the special circumstances of the region. (2) Purpose: (A) Senior agricultural science aims to cultivate high-level agricultural talents with knowledge and skills, so that they can actually produce, guide operations, promote agriculture, and provide a foundation for further research. (B) Senior industrial science aims to cultivate industrial talents and technicians' assistants with knowledge and skills, so that they can apply scientific methods to actual production, assist in promoting industrial improvement, and provide a foundation for further research. (C) Senior commercial science aims to cultivate commercial talents with knowledge and skills, so that they can understand the general trend of commerce at home and abroad, understand the opportunities for merchant development, and provide a foundation for further research. (3) Departments: (A) Agricultural science, such as agriculture, forestry, sericulture, animal husbandry, aquaculture, horticulture, etc., and may be divided or added as appropriate according to local needs. (B) Industrial science, such as machinery, electrical engineering, applied chemistry, dyeing and weaving, silk weaving, cotton weaving, wool weaving, civil engineering, construction surveying, etc., and may be divided or merged as appropriate according to actual needs. (C) Commercial science, such as banking, bookkeeping, accounting, shorthand, insurance, remittance, etc. (D) Home economics, such as sewing, embroidery, nursing, midwifery, etc. (E) Regarding other occupations, they should be established as appropriate according to local needs.

Second, Steps for Establishing Vocational Schools 208

In the past, the operation of vocational schools in our country has rarely achieved significant results. The reasons are nothing more than the lack of clear investigation and definite plans for the local environment, and often the lack of teachers, shortage of funds, and simple equipment, so that the talents cultivated, their knowledge and skills, cannot be as ideal as expected. Even if there are a few outstanding students, they cannot meet the needs of the environment, and they feel that it is difficult to find a way out. Therefore, we should be cautious at the beginning. The establishment of vocational schools should have prescribed steps so that graduates can truly serve the vocational industry, and then the purpose of vocational education can be achieved. The following are the proposed establishment steps:

As for the proposed change to run agricultural, industrial, and commercial departments, it should be submitted for approval after the existing classes are completely closed, depending on the financial and equipment situation. The Issue of Salary Demands by Teachers and Staff in Fujian Province Comes to an End 211

(Fuzhou Telegram) Since Zheng Zhenwen took over as the head of the Education Department in Fujian Province last winter, funding has become increasingly tight. However, in order to expand the department's business, the number of staff members in the department has increased from 54 to more than 90. In May, the head of the department personally went to Yanping and other areas to inspect, spending only 1,500 gold coins on travel expenses. The head of the department spared no effort to economize on all public funds. Recently, the province has accumulated more than three or four months of arrears in funding, and the schools have faced a difficult situation of being unable to cook without rice. Starting this month, the schools have been demanding salaries from the department. Recently, teachers and staff from various schools have been sitting at the Education Department to demand salaries. The head of the department came out to meet them, and there was a slight misunderstanding in the language, which led to a dispute. It is widely rumored that there is a strike, but this is not the case. It has now come to an end.

The Preparatory Committee for the Municipal Library, Museum, and Stadium Held Its Inaugural Meeting Yesterday; 20 Preparatory Committee Members Attended; Work Was Distributed to Various Groups and Sections 213

In order to prepare for the Municipal Library, Museum, and Stadium, the Municipal Government held the inaugural meeting of the Preparatory Committee for the Shanghai Municipal Library, Museum, and Stadium yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, convened by Mayor Wu, with more than 20 preparatory committee members attending. Work was distributed to various groups, and all matters of progress were discussed. The following are the details:

▲Attending Committee Members 214

The attending committee members included Ye Gongchuo, Zheng Hongnian, Liu Shiying, Guan Songsheng, Yu Qiaqing, Chen Guangfu (represented by Zheng Jianfeng), Ma Zongrong, Wang Yiting, Qin Runqing, Shen Siliang, Wang Yunwu, Dong Daqiu, Liu Haisu, Qian Xinzhi (represented by Liu Haisu), Cai Zengji (represented by Chen Jun), Li Zhaohuan, Shen Yi, Wang Xiaolai, Wu Yunzhai, Yu Hongjun, etc. Li Dachao and Lin Yannan attended as observers. Mayor Wu presided, and Lin Yannan took the minutes.

▲Mayor's Report 215

First, Mayor Wu Tiecheng reported, stating that it is necessary for Shanghai to establish a Municipal Library, Museum, and Stadium, and hoped that all preparatory committee members would work hard to promote the realization of these three major important constructions. In addition, the Municipal Hospital is also a matter of urgency, but it is planned to prepare for it separately. This preparatory committee will only discuss these three major important constructions, preparing a construction fund of 2 million yuan, including the Municipal Hospital. The stadium will require approximately 1.21 million, the museum 200,000, the library 200,000, and the Municipal Hospital 400,000. He requested that all preparatory committee members work separately. Subsequently, Yu Qiaqing, Ye Gongchuo, and others spoke successively, discussing the distribution of work. Afterwards, they went out of the room together and took a photo in front of the city government steps.

▲Distribution of Work 216

The preparatory committee is divided into three groups: economics, engineering, and administration. In addition to the three groups, there is also a design group, which serves as the hub of the business process. The economics group has eight members, and Qian Xinzhi, Qin Runqing, Chen Guangfu, Xu Shengchan, Du Yuesheng, Wu Yunzhai, and Yu Qiaqing were appointed to serve. The engineering group has five members, and Dong Daqiu, Zhang Xiaoliang, Zhao Shen, Guan Songsheng, and Liu Shiying were appointed to serve. The administration group has four members, and Wang Xiaolai, Shi Liangcai, Wu Kaixian, and Yu Hongjun were appointed to serve. The design group has one director, and Ye Gongchuo was appointed to serve. The design group is divided into three sections: (1) Library section, consisting of Ye Gongchuo, Wang Yiting, Wang Yunwu, Lu Feikui, Zheng Hongnian, Li Zhaohuan, and Ma Zongrong. (2) Museum section, consisting of Ye Gongchuo, Liu Haisu, Li Zhaohuan, Qian Xinzhi, Shi Liangcai, and Ma Zongrong. (3) Stadium section, consisting of Shen Siliang, Guan Songsheng, Zheng Hongnian, and Cheng Yize. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Chen Zixin's Enthusiasm for Labor Education 218

Chen Zixin, the manager of Hengda Cotton Mill in Yangsi Bridge, Pudong, is known for his enthusiasm for public welfare. Since assuming the position of municipal committee member of the Yangsi District, he has been praised by local people. Recently, in view of the fact that some young child laborers in the factory are engaged in labor, which is detrimental to their physical development, and considering that they are at the age when they should be studying, he built a school building on the remaining land of the Yangsi District Municipal Committee Office this summer and founded a worker's supplementary school. More than 100 young child laborers were ordered to stop working and enroll in the school to receive educational opportunities and work skills training. They are divided into two groups, A and B, according to their age. Group A graduates in two years, and Group B graduates in three years. After graduation, they are sent to work in the factory and receive higher wages. If their academic performance is excellent and they are aspiring to further their studies, they will be subsidized according to the school's scholarship program for further education. All children's books and supplies are provided free of charge by the school. To show consideration for the poor families of the students, each student receives a monthly subsidy of two yuan for household expenses. Those with fewer absences or excellent grades are subject to a separate bonus system. The school's expenses are all raised by Chen himself. The school opened on October 1st. In addition, for the male and female workers working in the factory, it is planned to set up separate classes according to the methods of the public schools, with two hours of reading per day. This is currently being planned. It is reported that the school has printed its articles of association to promote this effort, so that factory owners who are enthusiastic about labor education can request copies for reference.

The Loss of Four Provinces Affects Northeastern Students Studying Abroad. Qin Guoding Returns Home in a Distressed State. ▲ Carrying a Letter from the Consulate in Germany Requesting Relief from the Refugee Association. ▲ A Glimpse of the Economic Interruption Causing Financial Difficulty for Students Dropping Out of School in Germany. 219

Since the successive fall of the four northeastern provinces, the impact on self-funded students from the Northeast studying abroad has been significant, as all tuition and travel expenses have been cut off. This situation not only affects their studies, but also leaves some stranded overseas without a home. The Northeastern Refugee Relief Association in this city received Qin Guoding (from Liaoyang), a student studying in Germany, yesterday who was sent back to China by the Chinese Consul in Germany for the same reasons. The Consul specially issued a letter of certification, ordering him to request relief from the association. His situation is extremely difficult. The details are recorded below.

▲ The Journey Home 220

Qin Guoding, a student studying in Germany, is 22 years old and from Liaoyang, Northeast China. He graduated from Northeastern University at an early age and went to Germany at his own expense to study advanced industrial science at the University of Berlin. The planned study period was eight years. Since the September 18th Incident, followed by the postal blockade in the Northeast, Qin's expenses in Germany were exhausted. However, at that time, Qin did not want to drop out of school because his studies were not completed. He borrowed money from classmates and worked part-time in Germany to barely manage to graduate, and his situation was extremely difficult.

▲ Request for Relief 221

In August of this year (only one semester away from graduation), he was finally unable to make ends meet. He appealed to the Chinese Consulate in Germany, stating his situation. The Consulate then sent him back to China at its expense and, out of pity for his homelessness after returning to China, specially prepared a letter, instructing him to go to the Shanghai Northeastern Refugee Relief Association for assistance to avoid becoming destitute. Therefore, after arriving in Shanghai yesterday, Qin went to the association on Yunnan Road with the letter at 5:00 PM to request assistance. The Standing Director, Huang Bodu, met with him, offered comfort, and promised to provide relief. He also learned that the association would soon contact the Chinese Architects Association to arrange for him to apply his knowledge.

▲ Letter from the Consulate in Germany 222

The original letter from the Consulate in Germany is recorded below: "Dear Sirs, This is to inform you that Qin Guoding, a student from Benxi County, Liaoning Province, has studied architecture at the Higher Institute of Technology in Berlin for seven semesters. However, since the fall of the Northeast, his tuition fees have been cut off, and he has no home to return to. His situation is extremely pitiful. This Consulate has found a way to send him back to China. After the student arrives in Shanghai, we hope that your association will find a way to provide relief to avoid him becoming destitute. Your kindness will be greatly appreciated." The Northeastern Refugee Relief Association, Embassy in Germany, August 31st.

Students should focus on scientific research during their studies in order to acquire profound and useful knowledge. Today, your school is holding an awards ceremony to encourage students to work hard in their studies. Those who receive awards are glorious, and those who do not receive awards should work even harder and move forward actively, establish a foundation for their careers, and prepare to serve the entire Chinese nation.
