Temperaments of Northerners and Southerners 299

— Lie Huo

In the conversations of friends, there are often such jokes: "Foxes from Jiangnan," "Shan Dong brutes," "Hunan barbarians," "Jiangxi yokels," etc. Except for "Shan Dong brutes," which specifically refers to their large size, the rest seem to be able to be regarded as observations of temperament.

Speaking of temperament, in China, northerners and southerners certainly have their own temperaments, each province has its own temperament, and even different counties, a small region has its own special and distinctive temperament.

However, broadly speaking, we can summarize it with the two major systems of "north" and "south."

People who live in the north have these characteristics:

First, they are forthright. Han Yu said in his "Preface to Sending Off Dong Sheng": "Yan and Zhao have been known since ancient times for having many generous and tragic singers." This is indeed true. Northerners, whether speaking or doing things, are generally very forthright, not so fussy and circuitous, not speaking one thing and thinking another, not acting without regard to words.

Second, they are very conservative. To make a long story short, it is inevitable to involve social evolutionary history, that is, northern society undoubtedly still has a very strong feudal remnant. The characteristic of feudal society is conservatism, so northerners cannot escape the encompassing control of this social consciousness, and everyone is somewhat conservative. Not to mention major events, even in dealing with daily trivial matters, they often like to sing the tune of "Xiao Gui Cao Sui," following the rules and walking in the right path, unwilling to move forward with great strides and seek new gains.

Third, they are particularly particular about etiquette. This may originate from the fact that our old-brand sages were all produced in the north, and because our country's culture is based here, the dynasties have changed, and etiquette has been deeply engraved in the minds of ordinary people, not only becoming a habit, but simply becoming a kind of inherited temperament. When dealing with people, they all diligently reciprocate etiquette. If you say they are just hypocritical, they are not really, in short, northerners mostly have a characteristic of liking to talk about etiquette.

Speaking of southerners, they also have several prominent characteristics:

First, they are cunning. I often think that the saying "Foxes from Jiangnan" has quite a history. We know that foxes are cunning beasts, and the people of the Jiangzhe area are mostly not out of the category of white-faced scholars, oily tongues and slippery mouths, speaking one thing and meaning another, and putting on airs. This is probably due to the more advanced and complex society and the difficulty of living. Other factors such as beautiful mountains and clear waters and the nurturing of spirits also have a certain relationship. For example, the people of "Paradise Suzhou and Hangzhou" are particularly clever and cunning. In addition, the particularly developed commerce and the merchants are good at "fraud," which can also be regarded as having a considerable connection.

Second, they have a characteristic of adventure and initiative. This can be illustrated by two facts: one is that the adventurers who went abroad as overseas Chinese are almost all southerners from Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong; the second is the outbreak of revolutionary undertakings. To put it further, after more than two hundred years of Manchu rule, it was only Guangxi's Hong Xiuquan and his ilk who dared to rush forward, and although the matter was not successful, it was indeed a model. Then Mr. Sun Yat-sen came out to launch an uprising, and the Xinhai Revolution was able to succeed. Since then, the Northern Expedition of fifteen years, all the way to the present, can all explain the southerners. Standing on a certain position at the time, this initiative is a kind of bad temperament. But in fact, if you ask them to be quieter and more well-behaved, they really won't listen. They would rather have their heads cut off than not take risks. If they don't go overseas, they will rush into the country. This kind of restlessness and exploration of further progress is indeed necessary for social evolution.

Third, they are barbarous. For example, the people of Hunan, Guangxi, Yunnan, and Guizhou are prevalent with barbarism, a head-on confrontation, being tough is considered a good man. In geography textbooks, there is a narrative that "the people of Hunan are mostly barbarous." The "Sichuan Army," "Guangxi Army," and "Hunan Army" are all very famous, they just love to do this, if they do it skillfully, they will become great generals and heroes, and they don't think it is strange to fight tigers. This has a lot to do with the degree of civilization. In these provinces, there are still large numbers of Miao and indigenous people living intermixed. As for culture and literati, they are naturally relatively low and lacking.

The differences between the temperaments of northerners and southerners have been outlined above. Whether forthright or cunning, neither is a good phenomenon. We feel that in the same nation, there can only be a unified and beautiful national character, and there should be no temperament that varies according to the region. But our nation is actually like this, [illegible character] national character is not unified and beautiful, and the temperaments of various places are like this.

Page 22

intense development, no wonder "a heap of loose sand," "each scheming for himself." Where does the reason lie? (1) It cannot but be attributed to the inconvenience of transportation. There are no natural rivers running through the north and south (even a short canal is silted up), and there is no railway running directly through the north and south. What about highways is even more unnecessary to say. (2) Education is not universal, the illiteracy rate is above 80 percent, and there is no unified national language. Of course, there is a lack of tools and possibilities for contact and integration between people. To prescribe the right medicine, it depends on the keen understanding of those who plan for the country. Written in a pigeon cage-like small room on a night of autumn winds and autumn rains.

Mother and Daughter 300

— Lao San

After that talkative old woman had several conversations with Mrs. Lu in the Lu mansion, Miss Lu's marriage could be resolved with just one more matchmaking session, and at the same time, it would also relieve the burden that Mrs. Lu had been carrying on her shoulders for more than ten years.

Although it was a large Lu mansion with black walls, besides Mrs. Lu and Miss Lu, there were only the male and female servants hired by them. Mrs. Lu's husband, Mr. Lu, passed away very early, probably when Miss Lu was only two or three years old. Fortunately, he left them a house and a lot of savings, so there was naturally no problem with their livelihood. However, Mrs. Lu [illegible character] at that time, of course, she was still young Mrs. Lu, thinking about being widowed at a young age, she tried to commit suicide several times. Mrs. Lu's mother was still alive, and she advised her daughter day and night, saying: "Although the son-in-law died so early, what he left behind is enough for you and your daughter to spend. This girl will have a son to rely on in the future, isn't the mother herself like this? Young people, don't be so impetuous, it will make people laugh!"

Later, Mrs. Lu did not know whether it was for the sake of having a son to rely on in the future, or for fear of being laughed at? She painstakingly raised her daughter, Miss Lu.

Miss Lu grew to be fifteen years old, truly [illegible character] said to be as beautiful as a fish sinking and a goose falling, as beautiful as a flower closing under the moon, a lovely girl. Mrs. Lu saw that half of her hopes had been realized, and that the remaining money of Mr. Lu was still all spent on this daughter; she very generously sent her daughter to a girls' school to study, and Mrs. Lu actively did the work of the second half of her hopes.

However, the times were not the times, and everything changed when Miss Lu entered school. Making a fuss about cutting her hair was still a small matter, the clothes she made were all things that Mrs. Lu [illegible character] had never seen before, such strange clothes, but thinking that she only had this one daughter, she loved [illegible character] her, and besides, these kinds of clothes seemed to look especially beautiful on her daughter [illegible character].

Slowly, things changed again. Miss Lu never turned a hundred books every day when she came home, and she was always writing those messy letters with her head down, one after another, filling the paper box. Mrs. Lu herself was illiterate, and at first she thought it was homework from school, but later a tailor who often came in and out of her home accidentally discovered that there were many words of brothers and sisters crying on it. Only then did Mrs. Lu become anxious, her lovely daughter, don't be driven away by those wild men, so she locked her daughter up at home, not allowing her to go to school anymore, and on the one hand, she accelerated the process of inviting matchmaker Wang Ma to her home to discuss secretly, entrusting her grandmother to find a husband for Miss Lu, and promising a heavy wish.

As the saying goes, under heavy reward, there must be brave men. Wang Ma's pair of arm-like feet ran in and out of the black walls of the Lu mansion dozens of times, and it was agreed that a son was the only child of a silver shop owner. He was so good-looking, he and Miss Lu were a perfect match, and he had graduated from some university, and his family was rich, of course, there was no need to say. As soon as she opened the silver box, Mrs. Lu smiled with joy. However, the man's family wanted to see the young lady. In Mrs. Lu's opinion, what did my daughter have to compare to others? She didn't want to do it in such a strange way, giving her spoiled daughter to others to watch like a commodity. Of course, Wang Ma's feet were needed again, but the man's family insisted on seeing the young lady first. Wang Ma's good-talking mouth said a lot, what kind of family, what kind of family, she did the matchmaking, everyone matched before seeing each other, and then what nowadays, young ladies and young masters have to see each other themselves, so that they don't complain about their parents in the future. Mrs. Lu was moved by her words. Now that it was so, she made an appointment for a day to let herself see what kind of person the son-in-law was.

Wang Ma ran back and forth for more than a month [illegible character] on [illegible character] auspicious day [illegible character] ran out the date for the matchmaking, the two families [illegible character], made an appointment to watch a play in the theater [illegible character]. [illegible character] Tan [illegible character] [illegible character] [illegible character] [illegible character] [illegible character] [illegible character] [illegible character] [illegible character] [illegible character] On the family side, although there were only two people, mother and daughter, they had very different opinions. Miss Lu was a female student who had studied, and she didn't want anything to do with this kind of playboy-like silver shop scion. Mrs. Lu thought that as long as the son-in-law's face was not missing an eye or a mouth, what made her ten thousand times willing was that the family opened a silver shop, and she had lived her life for the sake of having a son to rely on. How could she let go of such a son-in-law lightly, so the mother and daughter argued day and night, and Wang Ma listened for news three times a day. . . . . . .

When Will Black and White Be Clearly Distinguished? 301

— Yin

Since [illegible character] practiced playing the qin and came out, passing by XX Road, I saw a long snake-like line of many rickshaws, next to the rickshaws stood men wearing tattered old blue cloth shirts, with their sleeves rolled up high and their trouser legs also rolled up high, wearing straw sandals, they were extraordinarily quiet, waiting like they were on trial. I didn't know the riddle in it, so even though I had passed this large group of rickshaws, I turned back to see what it was all about. Ah! It turned out to be an XX Rickshaw Company. At the main entrance there was a round thing similar to a table, with pencils and paper on it, and next to it stood a tall "foreign master," writing something I didn't know. Next to the "foreign master" was a short, thin, and bony Chinese man, wearing a green [illegible character] uniform, holding a stick in his hand, this was probably the so-called "foreman." A yellow-faced rickshaw puller pulled a rickshaw out, passing between the two men of particularly disparate height, he walked slowly, trembling. As he passed the Chinese foreman, the foreman glared at him, raised the stick in his hand, and blocked the rickshaw's path. Then, he diligently opened the rickshaw box, looking at the "foreign master" with a kind look, waiting for the "foreign master" to examine it sideways. The short, yellow-faced foreman looked up at the foreign master's breath, his attitude was really strange. Only when the "foreign master" slightly nodded his head did the foreman wave the stick violently. The rickshaw puller seemed like a prisoner released from the criminal court, and desperately ran away. The same rickshaws were all subjected to the same inspection. (Actually, I don't know what they were inspecting, I really don't know). After the inspection, the rickshaws lined up in an orderly fashion in front of the company's gate, the rickshaw pullers, all with their hands tied, were waiting outside the gate for the second trial, the second "order" of the "foreign master" like obedient sheep.

This phenomenon has gone from being special to becoming commonplace. But the rickshaw puller, with his two strong legs and a body full of stinky sweat, protecting the one or two mao he earned, he seemed to have no idea that he had cheaply sold his entire body and soul to obey the "foreign master's" orders. But when the customer exploits him for one or two cents of his leg money, he will show his eyes, scold him angrily, and give him a white eye, not to mention adding the respectful phrase "Your mother's?"

Here, we also say like Mozi, "…Now there is a person here who sees little black and white ink, but sees a lot of black and white: then this person will be regarded as not knowing the distinction between black and white. Taste little bitter, call it bitter: taste a lot of bitter and sweet: then this person must be regarded as not knowing the distinction between sweet and bitter.

Family Letters and Love Letters 302

— Kai Yu

I have lived the life of a student for over a decade. If I were to compare the attitudes of students towards their families and towards their lovers over these ten-plus years, I might be able to write a small booklet. However, time never permits me to do so, so I will start by discussing family letters and love letters.

Words are symbols of language, which no one can deny. Letters are written using words, and naturally, they are for exchanging information. However, even though they are both letters, students write them differently depending on whether they are family letters or love letters. When writing love letters, it seems like the words are alive, flowing endlessly. But when it comes to family letters, the words become dead, and they remain silent. Just looking at the bookstores now, elaborately bound love letter collections are becoming more and more common, while family letters are as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns, which proves everything. Love letters flourish, family letters decline – perhaps this statement can become a law, at least in the student world today. Without empty talk, let me cite a classmate's experience as evidence:

A certain classmate said that when he writes love letters, he always writes endlessly, not only in large quantities but also of high quality. He said that one night, after the sleep bell had already rung, and all the students were preparing to sleep, he lit a candle and wrote a thousand words, from acquaintance to first love, from first love to passionate love, from passionate love to kissing and hugging... Before he knew it, he had written more than two-thirds of fifty sheets of paper, and when he finished, he still felt a lingering regret that the paper was too short to express his feelings. However, when he writes family letters, he feels dry and tasteless, and other than "I am currently in financial straits, please remit ○○ yuan immediately," he has nothing to say. He said that he had inquired about this situation from many students in love, and the results were all the same. Now he wants to implement a method of using printing to replace family letters with several classmates. When writing, they only need to fill in the blanks, saving the time to write more love letters. It is truly killing two birds with one stone. The letter format is as follows:

"Dear Parents: Your child is currently experiencing financial difficulties. Modern Celebrity Paintings and Calligraphy

Mr. Zhu Lesan's Ink Plum Blossom (Brief Biography) 303

Zhu Lesan, courtesy name Xizhai, also known as the Nanyu Mountain Man, is a native of Xiaofeng, Zhejiang. He loves poetry, is skilled in seal carving, and paints in the style of seal script. He has received awards. Mr. [blank] closely [blank] resembles his teacher.

I hope you will remit ○○ yuan to alleviate my urgent needs. I respectfully request

Blessings. Your child, ○○, respectfully reports on ○ month ○ day."

From my observations as a student, what a certain classmate reported is all true. As for using printing to replace family letters, perhaps it can only be found in a certain gentleman and his several classmates. However, if you [blank] gather [blank] family letters and compare them with the above letter format, I think the difference will be at most fifty steps to a hundred steps away.

When parents see the above facts, they will inevitably cry out in unison. When lovers see it, they will certainly grin and laugh. One laugh and one cry are as different as heaven and earth. But parents, don't panic! Watch quietly. Lovers, a turn of the body becomes father.

Amateur Mailbox 304

Editor Sir:

I am a young woman approaching adulthood. Two years ago, I happily graduated from elementary school and was planning to enter higher primary school. Unfortunately, my father's business failed, and he declared bankruptcy, becoming utterly destitute. Therefore, I dropped out of school. After dropping out, in addition to working, I spend my free time reading books and newspapers to increase my knowledge. I enjoy reading your column the most, and I admire your answers immensely. Now I also have an urgent question that I would like to trouble you to guide me on.

My only mother, who loved and cared for me in this world, has passed away, and my father is also old. I have no hope of relying on my parents in the future. But as I grow older year by year, I still have no skills for making a living. Therefore, I am eager to find a proper position to learn a skill as a foundation for my future life. But I don't know what kind of profession is a proper profession for women. Like movie stars, I have no talent and cannot do it. I am not qualified to be a clerk in foreign firms, organizations, or banks, and I cannot handle it. Company and store clerks have a bad reputation (i.e., "flower vase"), and I am not very willing to do it in my heart. Ah! I am confused! I really have no way to think of it. I can only ask you, sir, for guidance. Please answer me! Sir, I wish you

Good health. Respectfully, Ouyang Huizhen

X X X X

Editor's Note: Miss Ouyang, because her mother is deceased and her father is old, she is concerned about the future and has no security in her life. She wants to find a suitable profession to support herself. This is very reasonable and very necessary. In fact, even if a woman does not have Miss Ouyang's kind of circumstances, she also needs to find a profession. In this era of fierce competition for survival, no nation can allow at least half of its women to only consume and not produce. Even if women are not considering their individual or family life, they should also consider the economy of the entire nation and engage in production. There are many consumers and few producers, and this situation cannot be sustained.

Miss Ouyang, because she does not have the talent for professions such as movie stars, does not dare to try. For clerks in organizations, foreign firms, banks, etc., because she cannot handle it, she does not dare to act rashly. This shows that she has a good understanding of herself. Originally, whether we are male or female, we must never gamble and risk trying things that do not suit our talents or that we cannot handle, because in the end, we will inevitably be eliminated. It's like using a stone mortar to act in a play, putting in a lot of effort but getting no good results. As for you saying that some professions have a bad reputation like "flower vase," so you don't want to do it, this is wrong. We should know that this kind of unpleasant argument, besides the speaker losing their personality, does not cause us any loss at all. Moreover, in this era of advocating women's professions, we need a large number of women with a great fearless spirit to fight against these vandals. After women's professions become widespread, and after women's professions have considerable achievements, this kind of demon will naturally retreat.

Drama

War and Peace (May Fourth) (Four-Act Play) 305

— Ling He

Act IV: Praise of Peace

Japanese Soldier C: (Enters from outside) Report! The company commander ordered me to tell you to quickly search every house. It's getting late, hurry back to the city! (Exits)

Japanese Officer: (Orders Japanese Soldier A) Then you take this group of bastards to the ancestral hall over there and wait until we catch more bandits and take them all back to the city.

(The Japanese officer orders the Japanese soldiers and youths A, B, C, and D to leave. The women and children are frightened and cry.)

Security Team A: Zhou Sanye, what's going on now? Our guns have been confiscated, and our superiors will beat us when we go back.

Village Chief: There's nothing I can do.

Security Team B: No, we were brought here by you, so you are responsible now.

Village Chief: How can I be responsible for this? You were just unlucky to run into Japanese soldiers. There's nothing anyone can do. When the Japanese soldiers attacked Shenyang, even young Marshal Zhang did not dare to resist, let alone us?

Security Team A: We don't care, we want Zhou Sanye to be responsible. We can't go back without guns.

Village Chief: That's not true. Go back boldly. If your superiors want to punish you, you can ask them. If they were in this situation, what could they do? Surely our three lives are not as important as three guns, right? ... Old woman, come and collect this corpse. It stinks a lot here, it's awful.

Middle-Aged Woman B: Bullshit! You can just kill someone and be done with it?

Village Chief: What do you want? (Emphasizing)

Middle-Aged Woman A: We want your life.

Village Chief: Bullshit, do you recognize this master?

Crowd A: We recognize you as a skinny dog.

Crowd: Down with him! Beat this skinny dog!

Village Chief: Come on, fire!

Security Team A: Where are the guns?

Village Chief: Oh? (Wants to escape)

(Woman B first grabs the village chief's collar and slaps him several times. The crowd swarms up, hitting and kicking. The two security team members are also beaten badly. Soon, the three are tied up and kneel in the center of the stage, their faces covered in blood.)

Young Woman: Damn it, you have this day too.

Middle-Aged Woman A: We have been bullied enough by him, and now he is kneeling in front of us. Is there anyone here? Let's all bite off a piece of his flesh.

Village Chief: Heavens! I can't take it. Everyone, do a good deed, and the Bodhisattva will bless you. (Knocks his head)

Young Woman: Now you want to ask the Bodhisattva?

Crowd B: Who has a knife? Kill him! Keeping him will only harm us later.

Village Chief: God, do a good deed!

Crowd A: No, first he has to burn all our IOUs.

Crowd B: Good, his land deeds should also be burned.

(Suddenly, there is a dense burst of gunfire, followed by a landslide-like loud sound.

Middle-Aged Woman A: Oh, the war has started again.

Crowd A: This must be the volunteers fighting the Japanese soldiers.

Young Woman: Then let's go quickly. What are we doing here? They will be fighting over here soon.

(Everyone scatters. The old man's body is also moved offstage)

Village Chief: Hey, please let me go!

Crowd: Bah! (Gunfire)
